Public Telegram 79

A Public Telegram from Chuansha Asking for Disaster Relief to all Major Charitable Organizations and Philanthropists Nationwide: The Chuansha County has been unlucky and suffered a devastating typhoon, which wreaked havoc. Yuansha, Yuanyuansha, and other places, islands formed by silt in the sea off our county, are often hit by huge tides. This time, on September 1st, a sudden typhoon caused violent waves to surge, as if overturning mountains, causing the embankments to collapse and the entire island to sink. Houses were washed away, and there were few survivors. The numbers of people and livestock drowned are impossible to count. The disastrous calamity is unlike anything seen before. There are 2,000 households and nearly 10,000 people affected by the disaster. Now, although the typhoon has passed, the water has not completely receded. The disaster victims are gathered on the embankments, without houses to live in or food to eat, crying from hunger and cold, searching for relatives and companions, displaced and miserable. The cries of grief shake the heavens. In addition, the bodies of dead people and livestock have not yet been completely buried, and the stench is spreading, which will breed an epidemic. If relief is not provided urgently, there will be no survivors. Such a disaster is almost inhuman. Those who are spared share the same roots. To help those in difficulty and alleviate hardship is the principle of Zhou ritual, and to share in disasters and relieve suffering is human sympathy. We are heartbroken and grieved, hating that we have no ability to save all who are starving, and therefore imploring those who have the means to help. We respectfully request that you organize a relief committee to speak up for the poor. We believe that the benevolent gentlemen and philanthropists of our country will be deeply sympathetic to this tragic situation. We beg you to provide urgent relief to the disaster victims, who are in imminent danger. Your support is as crucial as a spark to dry tinder. We beseech you to show pity for the dying swans and undertake a charitable act. Please quickly provide donations of money or goods, or solicit donations from friends and relatives. Even a few leaves of shade from the mulberry field can become a great tree, and a spoonful of water from the ocean can become sweet rain. Help the dying and give flesh and bones to the dead, so that we can build the merit of three generations together and save those in danger, becoming the living Buddhas of ten thousand families. Li Leng, the County Magistrate of Chuansha, and the Chairman of the Relief Committee, and the entire committee bow and stamp their seals.

A Telegram Received. Shanghai Qipan Street Shen Bao Office: Chiang, Ma, Cheng, Fan, Zhang, Yang, and other bandit gangs, totaling over ten thousand people, have invaded the county, entrenched along the banks of the Sha River and the areas of the old county, Shiligou, Dahuangmiao, Guangwumiao, Cishengji, Lixingji, Huji, Gaimiao, Zhangcedian, Sanjiadian, Kuitaiji, Banqiaoji, Yuanyouji, and Anfengji for over twenty days. They have plundered and killed, causing countless deaths and injuries among the people, and almost no livestock remains. The county territory is vast, over a hundred li, and has been ravaged by the bandits several times. Except for the First District, which has a few survivors, the remaining four districts have been completely devastated. The disaster area is vast, and the survivors are crying out in misery, with no hope of survival. They are desperately in need of rescue. In addition to raising funds locally and sending a telegram to the provincial government requesting emergency relief funds, we earnestly request that you promote this widely and solicit donations on our behalf. We hope that your mighty pen will sprinkle the willow branches of mercy, so that even small contributions can accumulate into a great sum, supporting our survivors. We urgently appeal to you. The Anhui A He County Bandit Disaster Relief Committee kowtows.

A Dispatch from Dihua: Luo Junren, Minister of Foreign Affairs and Minister of Judicial Administration, is touring Xinjiang. The Zhenyi Record has published two diary entries detailing the situation in Lanzhou. Luo has now arrived safely in Dihua on the 2nd and had fruitful discussions with the military and political authorities of Xinjiang Province. Here is a further description of the events.

(15) A Brief Tour of Lanzhou 80

August 31st was an unusually sunny day. We prepared to continue our journey west at 8:00 AM, but as the luggage was being loaded, the airport reported that there was damage to the aircraft parts and that repairs were needed, so we could not fly today. So, we had to stay in Lanzhou for another day. Minister Luo was accompanied by Chairman Zhu Shaoliang, Director Deng Shiyi, and the heads of various departments to tour the famous scenic spots of Lanzhou. I and Lin and Wang went to see the Yellow River Iron Bridge in the morning. The bridge was built 20 or 30 years ago and cost over 200,000 yuan at the time. Now, it would cost more than a million to build. Transportation across the river is all done using bullskin rafts and sheepskin rafts. The bullskin rafts are made of dozens of whole cowhides, each sewn into the shape of a cow with cow and sheep wool, and then arranged in several rows or dozens of them, covered with bamboo strips. The sheepskin rafts are smaller, made of only a dozen sheepskins linked together. Each sheepskin is filled with air by hand and plugged with wool, so the sheepskin rafts are faster, while the bullskin rafts can carry more. The people of Gansu transport goods for export by water, using rafts to travel downstream, which is very fast. However, it is difficult to travel upstream, so they have to carry them back. In the afternoon, we visited the Five Springs Mountain. The mountain has five springs, hence the name. In fact, it is connected to the White Pagoda Mountain and is one mountain. The trees on Five Springs Mountain are lush and green, very different from the barren yellow earth of other mountains. The climate inside the mountain is very cool and refreshing. If you are talking about escaping the summer heat, then even the mountain residences of Kuling are not far off. At 3:00 PM, Chairman Ma Qing called a theater troupe to the People's Education Hall and invited Minister Luo to listen to the play. At 6:00 PM, he hosted a banquet. Minister Luo had a long and pleasant conversation with Chairman Ma.

(16) Welcome in the Suburbs of Liangzhou 81

September 1st was a day of clear skies and ten thousand miles of cloudless sky, truly ideal weather for flying. At around 7:00 AM, we took a car from the provincial government to the airport. Chairman Zhu, Chairman Ma, Director Deng, the heads of various departments, the President of the High Court, and all the important people of the province, as well as military police bands, went to the airport to see us off. At 8:30 AM, we took off. We originally planned to go straight to Xinjiang Province, but the military and political authorities, people's organizations, and groups from Liangzhou and Ganzhou sent telegrams insisting that we stay for one night, so we could not delay along the way. At 10:00 AM, we arrived at Liangzhou Longluo Airport. Ma Buqing, Commander of the 1st Cavalry Division, led soldiers and County Magistrate Xu Guyuan led the people to welcome us. They insisted on inviting us to visit the city, but because the distance was too far and time was limited, we did not go. Immediately, a welcome rally was held on the welcome platform set up at the airport. County Magistrate Xu and representatives of various circles, Mr. So-and-so, first delivered welcome speeches, expressing their gratitude for the central government's concern for the Northwest. Minister Luo also gave a speech of encouragement, urging the people of all ethnic groups to live in equality and harmony and work together to strengthen the country and promote the prosperity of the Northwest. After the meal, we hurriedly flew west at 11:00 AM. Liangzhou is now called Wuwei County. It used to have a population of over 100,000, but after the 17th year earthquake and years of military disasters and famines, it now has only tens of thousands.

(10)(7) Donkey Cart Bumps to Suzhou 82

Passing Liangzhou and looking west, the Qilian Mountains stretch endlessly. The mountain peaks are covered in snow that gradually melts. Looking east, there is a vast, boundless desert. The journey by car is quite rough. Arriving at Lanzhou at 3 PM, the airport is about forty miles from the city, a desolate expanse of yellow sand. It's frighteningly desolate. Except for a few words on a mound of earth at the north end of the airport, the station consists of only two simple tents set up by the welcoming party, barely enough space to stand. After entering the tent to rest and drink tea, Qin Sheng-san, Chief of Staff sent by Ma Bu-kang, the Brigade Commander of the First Brigade of the Second Cavalry Division, and County Magistrate Wei Yu-xuan, among others, insisted on inviting us to the city. Their hospitality was irresistible, and since the plane could not fly that day, Minister Luo and I went along, while Mr. Lin Wu-er remained at the airport. The donkey cart rumbled incessantly, causing endless shaking. I felt dizzy, my head swam, and my intestines nearly burst. We didn't arrive in Suzhou city until 6 PM. Soldiers, police, and students were all lined up outside the city to welcome us. After arriving at the guesthouse, I met and talked with Brigade Commander Ma Bu-kang. After dinner, at 8 PM, we returned to the city gate by donkey cart, not reaching the airport until around 1 AM. The round trip of eighty miles took eight hours, leaving me both mentally and physically exhausted. I fell into bed and was almost unconscious. Suzhou is now called Jiuquan County, named for a spring within the city that contains wine. It is about sixty or seventy miles from the Qilian Mountains and receives no rain throughout the year. Cultivation relies entirely on snowmelt from the mountains for irrigation, so the stronger the sunlight, the more abundant the snowmelt, as if the sunlight were replacing rain. The main produce is wheat. Jiayu Pass is only thirty miles from the city. The area outside the pass, in Yumen County, has abundant coal oil, flowing everywhere. It can be scooped up and used for lamps, but no one develops it, leaving valuable goods discarded on the ground. It's truly a pity. The climate in Suzhou is very hot during the day, like sweltering humidity. Even wearing a single layer feels too thick, while the mornings and evenings are bitterly cold, like harsh winter. Even leather clothes don't feel warm enough, typical of a desert climate. There are no precise population statistics. A survey in the 15th year of the Republic stated there were fifty to sixty thousand residents, but there are fewer now.

(10)(8) Brief Stop in Hami, Meeting the Uyghur King 83

On September 2nd, at about 5 AM, I was groggily awakened by Mr. Lin and Mr. Wang. I was so stiff I could hardly get up. After Mr. Lin's strong encouragement, I managed to leave the bed. At 6 AM, we boarded the plane heading west. The morning air was clear, and the flight was very smooth. At 8:30 AM, we arrived in Hami. The entire route from Suzhou to Hami is desert, and Hami city is built in the midst of this desert. I had previously arranged to meet Ma Zhongying in Hami when I was in Lanzhou. Upon reaching Suzhou, I received a telegram from Zhang Feng-ming, the Hami Defense Commissioner, informing me that Ma was in Turpan and inviting Minister Luo to meet him there. Those who welcomed us at the Hami airport included Zhang Feng-ming, the City Defense Commissioner, He Ding, the County Magistrate, and Zhang Yan-ling, the Chief of Logistics from Ma Zhongying's forces, who had come from Turpan, as well as dozens of others. The Hami Uyghur King, Niezier, and his son, Bo-xi-er, were also present. The Uyghur King's official title is "Hami Local Mongolian Hereditary First-Class Zasake Double Prince." His son, Bo-xi-er, is currently serving as the Turpan City Defense Commissioner. After disembarking from the plane, Zhang Yan-ling, Ma Zhongying's representative, reported to Minister Luo that Ma could not come to Hami due to the importance of defense. He also requested that Minister Luo visit Turpan. Minister Luo explained that due to unexpected delays along the way, he had been away for a long time, and the Eurasia No. 1 plane needed to return to Shanghai. He had to go to Dihua first and would arrange a meeting in Turpan after arriving there. Zhang and others then invited Minister Luo to tour Hami city and collect taxes. Hami city is about three miles from the airport. A short car ride brought us there. First, we arrived at the guesthouse where Minister Luo and the Uyghur King had a long conversation. The Uyghur King first recounted the suffering the Uyghur people had endured from oppression. Minister Luo then conveyed the central government's kindness, stating that the Three Principles of the People advocated by the Premier stressed that all ethnic groups within the country were equal. The central government was also vigorously implementing this policy, showing deep concern, and would strive to improve Xinjiang's politics and stabilize order, ensuring equality for all ethnic groups, complete religious freedom, allowing people to live in peace and work happily, and jointly seek prosperity. After listening, the Uyghur King said that he had previously lived in darkness but today had the honor of seeing Minister Luo's esteemed face and hearing his teachings, as if seeing the light of day. He would guide the Uyghur people to obey the central and local governments. During the conversation, the Uyghur King also presented a memorial, written in the Uyghur language, awaiting translation. Various community leaders and all the Uyghur people in Hami city also presented memorials and requested an audience with Minister Luo. Minister Luo, accompanied by the Uyghur King, Zhang Yan-ling, and Zhang Feng-ming, left the guesthouse. The Uyghur people knelt to express their suffering. Minister Luo comforted them kindly, and the Uyghur people were moved to tears. Afterward, he toured the city with the Uyghur King and others.

(10)(9) Talking About the Uyghur City 84

Hami has three cities... where people live, Uyghur... are also mixed among them... originally... where troops were stationed. One is the Uyghur City, where the Uyghur King resides. Many other Uyghur... people live in the mountains... This... originated in Hami. The feelings between the Uyghur and Han people in Hami are difficult... to reconcile. Military and political... power is entirely in the hands of Han people... Many Uyghur... people are treated... in a way that has long caused resentment. When Jin Shuren initially implemented his new policies, things were peaceful. However, in the 20th year of the Republic, Jin Shuren abolished the Uyghur King's hereditary... position. Due to improper handling, Hami was divided into three counties, and... Uyghur... cultivated land was given... to Han people to cultivate, leading to extreme backlash and a conspiracy to revolt. Representatives were sent to contact Ma Zhongying, stationed in Gansu, to request military assistance. The Xinjiang... unrest began here. At the beginning of the incident, the old Uyghur King of Hami had just passed away. After the current Uyghur King took office, he went to the provincial capital to express his gratitude. Jin Shuren immediately detained him... The Uyghur King has always been extremely... kind to the Uyghur living in the mountains, who have long been dissatisfied. Seeing the situation, the Uyghur King urgently went to the provincial capital to request protection... whether this is right or wrong remains to be investigated. After the Hami incident occurred, the war continued until this spring when it finally... ended. Details of the events will be described later. However, the three cities of Hami have been devastated by this turmoil. When we inspected the cities, we saw ruins and rubble everywhere, a terrible sight to behold. In particular, the Uyghur City was completely deserted, a... barren land. Minister Luo, in order to convey the central government's kindness, specially used the central government's name to provide one thousand yuan to the Uyghur King to help... the disaster victims. The Uyghur King and the Uyghur people were moved to tears. Currently, there are several hundred households in Hami, of which about a dozen are Han Chinese. About three-quarters of the land is barren. King Niezier... is still planning to inherit the throne... this month. Some Uyghur... people are also against... the restoration. Hami is in the desert, and the climate is extremely... hot. The most famous product is the Hami melon. The melon is... round, quite similar to the honeydew melons of Beijing and Shanghai, but it tastes... much better... than others, and is four or five times larger.

(10)(20) Rocking in the Wind and Rain, Arriving in Dihua 85

After staying in Hami for about an hour, we flew west. It was expected that we would arrive in Dihua around 1 PM. However, when flying near Gucheng, we suddenly encountered strong winds and heavy rain. Near Dihua, the pilot... lost his way and circled the nearby mountains for an hour and a half. The situation was extremely dangerous and anxious. Fortunately, the pilot of the No. 1 plane was highly skilled, and at 2:45 PM, we landed safely at Dihua Airport. At that time, Dihua was experiencing heavy rain. The welcoming party and soldiers were soaked. The soldiers had arrived at the airport at 8 AM to line up, and had changed shifts three times due to the rain. Shortly after the plane stopped, Liu Wenlong, the Chairman of the Xinjiang Provincial Government, and Sheng Shicai, the Border Defense Commissioner, arrived by car to welcome us. We then rode into the city in the same car as Minister Luo and stayed at the Foreign Affairs Office. After a short rest, Liu and Sheng held a banquet at the office to welcome us, and we had a pleasant conversation. I was exhausted from the journey, so I rested at the office and decided to begin working with all parties the next day to stabilize the new situation. All parties in Xinjiang had been eagerly awaiting the arrival of a high-ranking central government official, so they greatly welcomed Minister Luo's visit to Xinjiang. For example, in the business community, hearing that Minister Luo had arrived immediately caused prices to fall significantly. They believed that Minister Luo's visit demonstrated the central government's concern for the border situation and that he would definitely assist the provincial government in resolving various difficulties and stabilizing the situation in Xinjiang.

(10)(21) Overview of the Current Situation in Xinjiang 86

The current situation in Xinjiang is generally stable. Ma Zhongying's forces have been absorbed by the provincial government and appointed as the Eastern Route Garrison Commander. However, southern Xinjiang remains isolated and communication is completely cut off. The most important issues currently facing Xinjiang are stabilizing the southern route and reorganizing finances. Xinjiang's currency system is extremely chaotic, and there is an absolute shortage of cash. Central government banknotes are not circulating, and market transactions rely entirely on provincial currency. The value of provincial banknotes fluctuates wildly every day. Today, the market rate is fifty provincial banknotes to one national currency. If the currency is not rectified quickly, Xinjiang's finances will collapse soon. Minister Luo will stay in Dihua for half a month to assist the provincial government in resolving all the difficult issues. His tasks mainly include witnessing the inauguration of Liu Wenlong as Chairman of the Provincial Government and Sheng Shicai as Border Defense Commissioner, discussing the organization of the provincial government, unifying the central government's diplomatic power, stabilizing southern Xinjiang, and reorganizing finances. Chairman Liu is experienced and cautious, with a deep understanding of the political situation. Commissioner Sheng is young and talented, with exceptional abilities. Xinjiang's future holds great promise. Minister Luo also plans to invite Ma Zhongying to visit the province to allow all parties to speak frankly and jointly discuss the aftermath. If Ma does not come, Minister Luo will personally visit Turpan. After meeting with Ma, he will travel to Yining to meet with Commander Zhang Peiyuan and inspect the border situation. Then, he will go to southern Xinjiang to comfort and appease... the Uyghurs to achieve the overall unity of Xinjiang. (Dispatch from Dihua, September 2nd)

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Convenes a Grain Management Conference 87

To Jointly Plan Relief for Rural Areas and Regulate Food Supply

Dispatch from Guling: Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, in order to regulate the food supply, has been actively promoting the storage of grain to fill granaries. Yesterday, he specifically sent telegrams to the provincial governments of Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Henan, Anhui, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Guangdong, and Shanghai, instructing them to each send a representative familiar with rural conditions and experienced in grain management to gather in Jiangxi before October 20th to jointly decide on measures. The telegram reads as follows: "Our country is founded on agriculture, and the grain issue is related to the people's livelihood, and also the foundation of the nation. In recent years, the situation in rural areas has been such that even in years of famine, hunger is inevitable, and in years of good harvest, grain prices fall, harming farmers. The farmers' pain is reaching... a breaking point, causing social unrest and crises on all sides.

Continued from Page 11 88

Page 11

The path to relief lies, first, in appropriately adjusting the surplus and deficit of grain in each province, blocking the intrusion of foreign rice; second, in storing half a year's worth of grain to prepare for times of famine and drought; and third, in activating rural finance to stabilize the drastic fall in grain prices. This year, the provinces along the Yangtze River have a good harvest in autumn, and it is imperative to take advantage of this favorable opportunity to comprehensively plan for the fundamental relief of rural areas. Therefore, several items are proposed for handling, with the following guidelines: (1) Jiangxi and Hunan provinces are both major rice-producing areas and should immediately seek ways to communicate with Guangdong and Shanghai, which have traditionally been grain-deficient areas. Consult with the authorities in those provinces and cities to encourage grain merchants to purchase grain from the Yangtze River region as much as possible to resist the transport of foreign rice to the interior. At the same time, the provinces along the Yangtze River should provide various conveniences to grain merchants from Guangdong and Shanghai to attract them. (2) Implement grain storage and restore the old system of local granaries. The Wuhan Headquarters repeatedly issued orders and sent letters to various provinces last year urging them to handle this matter. It should be checked and thoroughly implemented to achieve practical results. (3) It is proposed to request the central government to create new-style granaries in the provinces under the cotton and wheat loan program to handle rice storage, loan collateral, and coordinate transportation and sales to regulate the food supply, raise grain prices, and circulate rural finance. In the future, circulating funds will be vigorously assisted by the farmers' banks in the four provinces. By striving to move forward in accordance with the above guidelines, the essential plan to relieve the rural economy will not be just empty words. However, the details of this matter are very complex and difficult to handle. To seek practical results, it is necessary to gather experts for careful deliberation. It is hoped that each provincial government will send a representative familiar with rural conditions and well-versed in warehouse systems and grain management to gather in Jiangxi before October 20th to jointly discuss and decide on a method and implement it accordingly." (Datong News Agency)

Jiang Xiyuan Reviews the Guangdong Naval Fleet 89

丨Jiang and others also hold inauguration ceremonies丨

Dispatch from Guangzhou: After the Haiqi, Haichen, and Zhaohua warships came south, they were reorganized by Chen Jitang into the Guangdong Naval Fleet. I hope that in the future, all personnel will always check their work and not be unworthy of their positions. After the speech, they took a photo and then Jiang and the others returned to Guangzhou. (August 30th)

Hankou Postal Workers' Strike 90

Demanding Recognition of the Union and Implementing a Go-Slow

Postmaster Telegraphed the Head Office to Request Instructions

Dispatch from Hankou: The Hankou Postal Workers' Union was formally established in April of this year, having been approved and registered with the Central Party Headquarters, the Hankou Special Municipal Party Headquarters, and the Municipal Government. At that time, they requested recognition from the Hubei Postal Administration, but the Bureau ignored them, even refusing to accept letters. As a result, the union's affairs were greatly constrained. At the same time, the workers' treatment, in terms of allowances and clothing, was far behind that of the bureaus in Beijing, Shanghai, Tianjin, and other places, which caused resentment. Since there was much misunderstanding between the authorities and the workers, a labor strike was inevitable. On the 4th of this month, all postal workers held a temporary representatives' conference and invited Wu Shao-shu, a member of the Municipal Party Headquarters, to attend and provide guidance. It was decided on the spot to elect ten representatives, along with all the executive and supervisory committee members of the union, to petition the Municipal Party Headquarters and send representatives to negotiate with the Postmaster, immediately requesting formal written recognition of the union. The workers also attached the following requirements: (1) Hankou Bureau workers should receive the same treatment as Shanghai Bureau workers. (2) Following the example of unions in other places, the union should receive a monthly subsidy of one hundred yuan. (3) Union workers should be guaranteed and provided with convenience. At 1 PM on the afternoon of the 6th, all the representatives and committee members went to the Municipal Party Headquarters to petition. Wu Shao-shu and Yang Xing-qin, two committee members, received them, expressing sympathy for the demands. The Municipal Party Headquarters appointed Committee Member Wu and dispatched You Ding-yi, the director of the Civil Affairs Section, to accompany the petition representatives to the Post Office. Wu Shao-shu first negotiated with the Postmaster, Mr. Smith, explaining that the establishment of the Postal Workers' Union had been approved by the Central Party Headquarters and the Hankou Special Municipal Party Headquarters, making it a legal organization that should be recognized by the Bureau. He also pointed out that postal workers' unions in other places had been recognized and assisted by local post offices, such as in Beijing and Shanghai, as well as the nearby city of Changsha, which already had precedents. Why should Hankou be different? He repeatedly tried to persuade him, but Mr. Smith remained unyielding, and his attitude was even more stubborn than before, with no room for compromise on the workers' demands. Deputy Officer Liu of the Garrison Command tried to mediate but had no effect. All the workers of the Bureau believed that the Postmaster was extremely oppressive, and they were so indignant that they went on a spontaneous go-slow at 2:30 PM. The Police Department and the Third Special District Police Station, fearing an incident, immediately sent soldiers and police to the scene to maintain order. Postmaster Mr. Smith, seeing the workers' firm determination, softened his attitude and agreed to telegraph the Head Office for instructions, with a three-day deadline for a reply. He also signed to accept the union's official letter. Although the workers expressed dissatisfaction, they were persuaded by the officials and police to refrain from insisting. Thereupon, Wu Shao-shu announced to the crowd, asking them to resume work and wait for a resolution. Deputy Postmaster Liu Yao-ting also reported that the Bureau had no prejudice against recognizing the union, but it was just a matter of time. The union officials then advocated temporarily resuming work and waiting for a resolution. At 4:30 PM, all the workers resumed work. It was fortunate that the go-slow lasted only two hours. (6th)

Jiangsu Province Levies a Perpetual Tenancy Tax 91

Five Jiao of Silver Per Mu, Paid by the Perpetual Tenant

Dispatch from Zhenjiang: The Jiangsu Provincial Government held its 594th meeting the other day and passed the amended Jiangsu Province Regulations for Levying a Perpetual Tenancy Deed Tax, which are recorded below:

Article 1: Anyone who has tenancy rights on cultivated or pastoral land and enters into a contract for its transfer shall pay deed tax in accordance with the provisions of these regulations. The perpetual tenancy referred to in the preceding paragraph refers to what is commonly known as field surface, field pits, fertile soil, and the like. The perpetual contract referred to in this article refers to various perpetual tenancy agreements entered into in accordance with local customs, such as field surface deeds, transfer deeds, pre-agreements, and the like, which have the nature of perpetual tenancy. Article 2: The perpetual tenancy deed tax shall be five jiao of silver per mu, with fractional amounts calculated pro rata by mu, and shall be paid by the holder of the perpetual tenancy right. Article 3: Anyone who enters into a perpetual tenancy contract shall, within three months from the date of the contract, prepare the tax payment, submit the contract, and send it to the relevant county government for verification and registration, and be given a tax payment certificate. Article 4: For land with the nature of perpetual tenancy after the implementation of these regulations, if no contract has been entered into or the contract has been lost, a supplementary contract shall be entered into within three months from the date of promulgation of these regulations, and other certificates shall be attached and sent to the relevant county government for approval of tax payment and certificate issuance in accordance with the provisions of Article 3. Article 5: If the perpetual tenant fails to send the application for verification and registration and complete the tax payment deed within the time limit prescribed in Articles 2 and 2, he shall be ordered to pay the tax at the prescribed rate and shall be punished in accordance with the following provisions: (1) If the time limit is exceeded by more than three months, a penalty of two times the tax payable shall be imposed. (2) If the time limit is exceeded by more than one year, a penalty of three times the tax payable shall be imposed. Thirty percent of the penalty in the preceding paragraph shall be used to cover expenses, and seventy percent shall be paid into the treasury. Article 6: If the perpetual tenant violates the provisions of Articles 3 and 4 and delays in paying taxes, anyone may report to the county government with responsibility. After verification, thirty percent of the penalty fine shall be given as a reward. Article 7: Perpetual tenancy contracts that have not been verified, registered, and taxed shall have no effect as evidence in litigation. Article 8: The rules for levying the perpetual tenancy tax shall be separately determined. Article 9: No surcharges shall be levied on the perpetual tenancy tax for any needs of the county or local government. Article 10: These regulations shall be implemented upon promulgation by the resolution of the Jiangsu Provincial Government Committee.

Anhui Business Federation Requests Cessation of the Import Tax on Foreign Rice 92

Foreign rice imports encroach on the domestic rice market. Please levy taxes immediately to maintain the rural economy.

Dispatch from Wuhu: The Anhui Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation and the Wuhu County Chamber of Commerce believe that in recent years, domestic rice prices have been declining, and the rural economy has become universally bankrupt. Even the cities are on the verge of collapse. The reason is that foreign rice is rampant and occupies the market. Rice-producing areas are becoming overstocked, leading to this situation. For example, the Guangdong and Guangxi provinces have always been areas for Anhui rice sales, but now they have been almost entirely occupied by foreign rice. The only solution is to increase the import tax on foreign rice to protect the domestic rice market. Therefore, today (1st), telegrams were sent to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and the Ministry of Interior, requesting that they immediately adopt the suggestion of the five provincial governments of Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Henan to implement the increased import tax on foreign rice. The original telegram reads, "Respectfully to the Executive Yuan, Ministry of Interior, Ministry of Finance, and Ministry of Industry in Nanjing: Reports indicate that the five provincial governments of Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Henan have telegraphed the Central Government to implement an increased import tax on foreign rice to resist it and maintain the rural economy. This is welcome news, and it benefits all the people. We ask your esteemed Yuan to describe and present it in detail. Since foreign rice imports, they initially sold well in Guangdong and Guangxi, seizing our market, which could be considered a supplement to the famine in the south and was beneficial to the people's food supply. Later, taking advantage of the tax-free advantage of foreign rice, they dumped it into the coastal and riverine provinces, encroaching on our country's grain sales market, so that in the 20th year, after the great flood, the vitality of the disaster-stricken provinces was mostly not restored. They relied entirely on agricultural income to maintain their livelihoods, but rice prices plummeted, and the funds they earned from selling grain were not enough to pay for farming. Years of good harvest did not satisfy them, and banditry increased. The harm to farmers from cheap grain is pitiable. As for the landowners, the highest-yielding fields harvest one hundred forty to fifty catties of rice per mu, the next-best fields harvest seventy to eighty catties, and the next again harvest forty to fifty catties. The price of rice is two yuan per dan, but the taxes and local surcharges, as well as all the expenses for harvesting rice, amount to two yuan five to six jiao per mu, or at least one yuan seven to eight jiao. For fields flooded in spring or dried up in summer, even if not a blade of grass is harvested, the taxes, surcharges, and flood prevention costs cannot be avoided. It has long been the norm to compensate for abandoned fields. Therefore, families with land are all suffering due to the impact of cheap grain. Fields that were previously worth one hundred yuan per mu are now devalued to thirty to forty yuan, and no one will buy them. The reason is that foreign rice dumping has caused grain prices to fall daily. As a result, rural areas are bankrupt, purchasing power is weak, commercial markets are depressed, finance is stagnant, and workers are unemployed, all of which are affected. According to reports from chambers of commerce in various places, Anhui's rice and grain have traditionally been marketed in Guangdong, Chaozhou, Guangxi, and other places, but since foreign rice imports, they have been invisibly squeezed out, and sales have been shrinking daily. Recently, they have been selling at a lower price, promoting it in the Yangtze River basin, so that last year it was already a year of good harvest and famine, and this year's new grain is even cheaper, and the farmers feel even more pain. Recently, bandits have been active in Hanshan, and the farmers have been coerced to follow them, which is not unrelated to the pressure of making a living. Looking to the future, we cannot help but shudder. We can only telegraph your esteemed Yuan to observe that our country's rice and grain have been encroached upon by foreign rice, the sales value is falling daily, and all the people are affected, threatening a total collapse. Adopt the proposals of the five provincial governments of Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Henan to implement an import tax on foreign rice to save the situation and restore the people's livelihood. We cannot wait to be ordered. Wu Xingzhou and others, the chairman of the Anhui Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation and the Wuhu County Chamber of Commerce, respectfully salute you." (1st)

Southern Hui Dike Collapses, Causing Disaster 93

More Than a Thousand Households Submerged

Dispatch from Nanhui: A hurricane passed through our county the other day, with strong winds and heavy rain,

non-stop day and night, causing heavy damage everywhere. Because traffic was disrupted at the time and telephones were out of service, it was impossible to find out the details. Now, after investigating various places, we have learned that the eastern Xiang dike on the coastal road in the first district collapsed for more than thirty zhang, about four to five hundred zhang in the Zhunan and Wangtan two Xiang, and the dikes around Wanghailou in the Siquan area were damaged north and south for dozens of zhang. For a time, the tide rushed into the plains in each of these places, with water six to seven feet deep. Many houses collapsed, and people and animals were killed or injured. In the second district, the newly built set dike in Wuliuqi Tuan was washed away for twenty li north and south, and more than a thousand households were submerged. Many people and animals were also killed or injured. In the fourth district, the dike body from Ligongtang, newly opened port, to the Xihe port was breached, and the water cave collapsed. The Liuzaogang water cave collapsed for more than three zhang, and the dike body south of the cave collapsed for six to seven zhang. The newly built set dike collapsed for about ten zhang. The Dongligongtang and the newly built preparation dikes were also washed away for seven to eight zhang. The residents in that area barely escaped with their lives, suffering considerable losses, which were even worse than the floods of the 20th year. Now, the county party headquarters and the county government have received reports from various disaster-stricken areas. Yesterday, Zhang Longjiang, a member of the standing committee, and Yuan Xiluo, the county head, went down to the villages to survey the disaster and will decide on relief methods.

(September 6th)

江松 Villagers Seek Revenge and Commit Assault: Investigation 94

Zhang Shigen, a resident of the seventh Tu in Tinglin, a man in his prime, known for his aggressive nature, was an object of concern among his neighbors. He had a long-standing grudge with Fang Tongsheng and Fang Awu, two residents of Shanyang Town, for some reason. On the second day of the month, he conspired with Zhang Yousheng, hid small knives, and went to Shanyang to seek revenge on the Fangs. Upon seeing them, they immediately drew their knives and stabbed violently. The two Fangs were injured and fell to the ground on the spot. Fang Tongsheng suffered a severe knife wound to his waist. Seeing that he had caused trouble, Zhang Yousheng immediately fled. Zhang Shigen was apprehended by the Shanyang Defense Corps and sent to the county court for interrogation yesterday. The injured Fang Tongsheng and Fang Awu have been hired boats by their relatives and taken to the hospital for examination. Their injuries are severe, and there are concerns about their lives.

A Thug Blocks the Road and Rapes a Young Woman 96

Lu, a woman from Shen Dianqiao in Suzhou (also known as A'erbao), 23 years old, was returning home from Suzhou on the 6th. While passing near Shen Dianqiao, she was suddenly stopped by three thugs, Tian Shougen, Tian Jinpu, and Chen A'ansheng. Various Industries Oppose Tax Collection by Household 97

The Business Tax Bureau has repeatedly received provincial orders to eliminate the practice of business tax being handled by trade associations and to directly collect taxes from households. Wuxi Procuratorate Executes Two Kidnappers by Firing Squad 98

Weng Zhendong, a villager from Xue Dianxiang in the twelfth district of the county, was kidnapped by bandits on September 29th of last year and held for ransom. Subsequently, Zhu Meiji, the head of the eighth district's defense corps, apprehended the bandits Fang Laifu, A'shi, Xu Fengchi, Zhuang Shigen, and Shi Rengen, and rescued the victim. The five bandits were presented to the county government and transferred to the county court. The court sentenced Fang, Zou, and Xu to death. Later, because Xu only wrote the ransom letter on behalf of the others, the High Court sent the case back for a retrial. The cases of Fang and Zou were forwarded to the provincial government for approval by the High Court. The provincial government issued an order to the county court to notify them. Chief Judge Xu sent a letter to the Procuratorate for execution. Chief Prosecutor Zhou signed the order at 4:30 PM the day before yesterday to take the two prisoners for identification. He then sent Prosecutor Shen as the supervising officer to escort Fang and Zou to the south drill ground for execution by firing squad.

The Repercussions of Organizing a Stone Powder Trust 99

The two stone powder factories in this county, Chengtai and Chengda, produce more than 800,000 dan of powder each year, 80-90% of which is sold to rice mills. They can make a huge profit of 150,000 to 200,000 yuan per year. Last year, Hu Jia and other citizens from Nanli submitted a petition to the Ministry of Industry, requesting the county to strictly prohibit the addition of this stone powder to rice, as it was harmful to health. After receiving the petition, the Ministry of Industry forwarded it to the Health Testing Laboratory. The test results showed that it was not related to health, and its use was allowed. As a result, the business of the two factories became even more developed, while the light powder industry suffered a strong enemy and declined to the point of complete stagnation. Recently, the owner of the factory, Zou Chongfan, and others, seeing the huge profits involved, contacted the Shenchang and Ruichang powder factories in Shanghai and organized a stone powder trust, named Ruichang Cheng. It is expected to produce about 2 million bags of powder per year, with a profit of about 600,000 yuan. As for the raw materials used, they have signed a contract with the owner of Changxing Mountain to exclusively use white stone for 12 years, stipulating that it cannot be resold to other new factories. New regulations have also been set for the price of stone powder: retail price is five jiao per bag, no arrears are allowed, and new scales must be used. When stone powder is delivered to the rice mills, a handling fee and labor fee must be added. These new regulations were implemented on the first of this month. After learning about this, the rice mills and rice shops in the county protested one after another. They held a relief meeting at a rice shop in Beizhako, deciding that all rice mills would switch to using air blasting and not use stone powder for mixing, and advocating the restoration of light powder to resist.

A Tsunami in Lusi, Nantong, Causes Disaster 100

The coastal areas of Nantong were affected by tidal disasters due to the recent hurricane. On the 3rd, a tsunami occurred in Lusi. More than 40 ships were lost at sea, and fishermen lost more than 1,000 nets. The seawall collapsed, and the tide flooded in. The fields north of the Fan Gong Dike were more than 1 zhang deep and completely lost. Four percent of the fields south of the dike remained. The county government is currently handling the aftermath.

A Secretary at Hangzhou University Commits Suicide by Poisoning 101

Qian Zibin, who lived at No. 10 Shuicheng Bridge, Jianggan, Hangzhou, was 20 years old. His parents were both deceased. He used to work as a secretary at Zhijiang University. Recently, he returned home after losing his job. Facing economic difficulties, he conceived the idea of suicide. He bought poison and committed suicide the night before last (the 6th). His family discovered him and rushed him to Liuhe Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. He died yesterday (the 7th) morning.

Wang Yansong Suggests Actively Commemorating September 18th 118

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has forwarded it to the Central Government

All Sectors Extending Work Hours

Wang Yansong, a Standing Committee member of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, proposed that the national humiliation of September 18th should be commemorated with an active spirit. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce passed it and forwarded it to the Central Government for review and compliance. The original submission stated, "This is to request that the Central Government be requested to issue an order to the whole country to change all commemorations of the national humiliation of September 18th to an active method in order to achieve practical results. In his reasons, he stated that the number of national humiliation commemorations in our country is almost the highest in the world. Everything in politics, science, economics, agriculture, industry, and commerce is inferior to others, but only the number of national humiliations is the highest. This is truly a great shame and humiliation for our Chinese nation. However, in the past, all national agencies, groups, schools, and factories have not been able to commemorate each national humiliation day in a valuable and meaningful way. On this day, merchants close their stores for one day, workers stop working for one day, students stop studying for one day, and politicians take a day off. Those who commemorate more sincerely also hang half-mast flags to express their condolences and convene a memorial meeting in the morning, thinking that they have done their best to commemorate. They do not know that this kind of commemoration method not only wastes time and squanders time, but also goes against the legacy of perseverance and hard work, making the business of the business community for one day, the work of the factory for one day, and the studies of the students for one day, all thrown into nothingness. This is no different from active suicide. When I speak of this, I cannot help but tremble. Therefore, I hereby propose the following methods: Every year on the anniversary of the September 18th National Humiliation Day, (A) All national agencies and groups, in addition to hanging half-mast flags to express their condolences and holding memorial meetings, shall uniformly extend office hours. (B) All national schools, in addition to hanging half-mast flags to express their condolences and holding memorial meetings, shall uniformly increase teaching time. (C) All national factories, in addition to sounding sirens to express their condolences within the prescribed time, shall uniformly extend working hours. (D) The national business community should take this day as the National Goods Movement Day. In addition to hanging half-mast flags in front of their stores, each store should also post striking slogans promoting national goods to attract widespread attention from the society." After discussion, it was decided to forward the case to the Central Government for adoption. The case has been recorded and is hereby submitted to the Executive Committee of the Central Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang for verification. It is convenient for the public to review it and order compliance.

The Central Mint is Commended by Order 119

Since the Central Mint began minting new coins, it has been extremely careful about the tolerance, fineness, and weight of the coins in order to show credibility at home and abroad. Since Dr. Glader, an American consultant, advised the factory, the new coins of the factory were sent to the Philadelphia and San Francisco Mints in the United States for testing. It is said that the testing reports from the two factories have now been sent, and the results are very good. All the new coins are within the legal standard tolerance for fineness. The factory reported in detail to the Ministry of Finance a few days ago, and now it has been ordered to commend the factory and publish the matter in the gazette.

Silk Factory Workers' Attempt to Resume Work Yesterday Failed 120

It Affected Five Factories in the Concession Area

The Trade Union Exhorted Them to Resume Work

According to Xinsheng News Agency, after the female workers of the silk factories in the Zhabei Xinza District went on strike again to oppose the implementation of the quota system, the Social Affairs Bureau mediated in the last few days and set out three measures. Then, both parties were instructed to resume work uniformly yesterday. Unexpectedly, several factories did not sound their sirens, and the workers did not arrive at all the factories. The 21 factories successively resumed their strikes, and five factories, including Taixin in the Concession Area, were also affected. The situation is bad. The details are as follows:

Notice to Start Work 121

The Silk Factory Association issued a notice to the factories to start work, stating, "This is to inform you that the representatives of the Association received an order from the Social Affairs Bureau today that the trial implementation of the quota system should be handled by the Bureau. You are hereby ordered to notify all silk factories to start work uniformly tomorrow morning. The Bureau will also send a letter to the Public Security Bureau requesting them to send police to protect the factories." Shanghai Silk Factory Association Committee Chairman Shen Jianchen.

Situation of Starting Work 122

Since the Social Affairs Bureau ordered both parties to resume work uniformly by yesterday, the Sixth District Silk Workers' Union sent supervisors Yuan Yun, Yang Zhi, Hua San Shi, Wu Suzhen, and all the cadres to persuade the workers. At 5:45 AM, the female workers of each factory received a notice from the union and went to work as usual. However, the number of workers was not complete. Each factory also received a notice from the association to start work. However, six factories, including Ganyuan, Xiexin, Xiexing, Hongshengyuanxin on Changan Road, and Ruifeng on Meiyuan Road, did not sound their whistles to start work. Some workers in the remaining factories had already entered the factory to work, but some workers were still waiting to see. Because the workers outside were causing trouble, the factories that started work opened their doors to release the workers. However, Lao Jun said that the factories opened their doors to release the workers because the workers did not go to work in each factory, and there was no trouble. As a result, the resumption of work failed. The Fourth District Public Security Bureau added two police officers to each factory to protect them during the resumption of work. District Chief Lai Gang personally patrolled and inspected the factories.

Successive Strikes 123

There are a total of 21 silk factories in the Zhabei Xinza District. Six factories, including Ganyuan, Xiexin, Xiexing, Hongshengyuanxin on Changan Road, and Ruisheng on Meiyuan Road, did not sound their sirens to start work. Four factories, including Fuxing, Maofeng, Hongchun on Changan Road, and Yuanfengyong on Hengfeng Road, closed their factories and restarted work. Seven factories, including Chujiejiyu, Xieji Zhenxing Yuji on Changan Road, Wuxing on Meiyuan Road, Jiatay on Guangfu Road, and Yuanfengyong on Hengfeng Road, stopped their machines because of insufficient workers or because the workers did not enter the factories. Four factories, including Meifeng on Hengfeng Road, Jiyu Taiji on Gonghe Road, Maitai Jiji Third Factory on Changan Road, and Yuanxing on Yutong Road, continued to start work as usual. After the lunch break, only a few workers went to work, and the striking workers swarmed in the factories again, causing internal workers to be unable to work in peace. Because they were afraid that the workers would crowd people and cause tragedy, each factory took the initiative to stop work and open the doors to release the workers.

Impact on the Concessions 124

When the workers of various factories in Zhabei went on strike yesterday morning, they formed a group at 8 o'clock and attacked the Yu Yuan Silk Factory on Guóqìng Road in the concession area, causing disturbances for a long time. The factory workers, who were working, responded upon hearing the noise and immediately stopped working. Seeing the situation, the factory management knew it was difficult to suppress and immediately opened the gate to let the workers go home. The Yu Yuan workers then went to three factories, including Tai Yuan and Tai Ji, on Avenue Albert, spreading the news, causing the workers of the three factories to go on strike at the same time. The Xiang Yuan Factory on Gansu Road also voluntarily closed down upon hearing the news. As for Yihe on Chengdu Road, it was not affected because it was located further away. Fortunately, no incidents occurred north of the Xinzha Railway and in the Nanshi area.

Union Attitude 125

The silk reeling industry union in the three districts only learned about the incident at 1 p.m. They immediately sent supervisors Yang Shumei, Cui Abao, and others to persuade the workers separately, but it was already too late. At that time, they sent personnel to report to the Party and government organs and notified all factories to sound the whistle for work this morning, waiting for the union to persuade the workers to go to work. Yesterday afternoon, the silk reeling industry union in the six districts issued leaflets to all workers, advising them to return to work, saying, "Dear workers, why are we on strike this time? It is because we oppose the capitalists' changing to the production system. Now we must understand that after the union raised objections to the implementation of the production system, it has been submitted to the higher authorities for handling. The Social Affairs Bureau convened both labor and capital for questioning and decided not to implement it immediately. This problem can now be said to have been completely won. It is still treated as before, with a wage of 50 cents per day and a reward of 20 cents on Sunday for middle and small workers. For the sake of making a living, we should go to work as usual. Do not listen to others' instigation and cause misunderstandings, refusing to go to work. This is absolutely wrong. If you make such unreasonable noise, I am afraid the higher authorities will take action, wouldn't that be detrimental to yourselves? Workers, the union is the guarantee of the workers, it speaks for the workers, and it will never deceive the workers. You can rest assured and quickly go to work tomorrow and work with peace of mind. Continuing to strike day after day will cause you to suffer losses. Don't misunderstand. Now we are still making our own living. After this return to work, we will still be treated according to the previous method of paying wages on a daily basis. Everyone must understand this."

Soap Industry Uses Japanese Hydrogenated Oil 126

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Sends a Letter Requesting Persuasion to Stop

Yesterday, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Soap Industry Association, saying, "Dear Sirs, on the 5th of this month, we received a letter from the Hunan People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, stating that according to a joint report from soap factories such as Dasheng, Zhengda, Guangming, Jingsheng, and Zheng Guangming in this city, they had previously discovered that the soap shipped from Shanghai and Hankou to Hunan was all made by secretly purchasing Japanese hydrogenated fish oil. At that time, they reported to your association for verification, requesting that the anti-Japanese sub-associations in various counties be notified to pay attention to investigation and that the Shanghai and Hankou chambers of commerce be requested to conduct strict investigation and prohibition to prevent the dumping of enemy goods. Later, it was heard that the Shanghai and Hankou chambers of commerce all replied vaguely, not admitting that there was a situation of using fish oil to make soap, and they were indifferent to it, which is really infuriating. Fortunately, heaven does not hide evil, and a secret letter from the Japanese to various soap factories in Hunan was suddenly found, which was to contact them to secretly purchase fish oil. This is the conclusive proof that the Japanese secretly sell fish oil to Chinese traitors. The letter has been submitted to your association for verification. However, the soap factories in Shanghai and Hankou knowingly know that fish oil is an enemy product, but they secretly cooperate with dealers to make soap. They only want to promote sales and develop, only seeking profit, and completely ignore the fact that the national crisis is still pressing and the national humiliation is very serious. It also affects the promotion of domestic goods and the soap industry in Hunan. These traitors are truly unforgivable. I hereby send another letter requesting your association to conduct a detailed investigation immediately and strictly prohibit it, and also notify the anti-Japanese sub-associations in various counties of this province to conduct a thorough investigation and not allow stores to mistakenly sell it, so as to unite and eliminate enemy goods, which is truly in the public interest. It is found that the report of various soap factories is not false, and the impact on domestic products is indeed significant. It must be strictly investigated and prohibited. Based on the previous situation, a copy of the original document is enclosed and sent to your association. Please verify and reply. As for the intimate friendship, etc., a copy of the letter is attached to the association. It is found that a certain Japanese company is still trying its best to sell Japanese hydrogenated fish oil to soap factories in Hunan Province. Therefore, various soap factories in Shanghai are even more of a place for their attention. It is difficult to guarantee that there are no members of your association who are tempted by them. I hereby enclose a copy of the letter. I hope your association will secretly investigate whether any of your members privately use Japanese hydrogenated fish oil as raw material, and give a factual reply. At the same time, take measures to prevent it and earnestly persuade them to stop. This is our sincere hope."

Overseas Chinese General Association Requests Restoration 127

Yesterday, a Request was Submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau for Approval and Reorganization

Overseas Chinese in Mexico and Japanese Overseas Chinese Telegraphically Request Maintenance

Since its establishment, the Global Overseas Chinese General Association in this city has been able to do its best to maintain the interests of overseas Chinese at home and abroad. Recently, it was ordered to close down and stop activities by the authorities for publishing newspaper advertisements to raise donations to aid the Mexican refugees who were expelled and returned to China. Now it is learned that the association, in order to maintain the interests of overseas Chinese, specially submitted a request to the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday to forward it to the municipal government, requesting the Executive Yuan to comply with the feelings of the overseas Chinese and approve the filing so that it can continue to proceed. It is also learned that the Japanese Overseas Chinese Deportation Group and the Mexican Refugee Maintenance Association telegraphed Chairman Chiang of the Military Commission yesterday, requesting that he grant maintenance. The details of each situation are recorded as follows:

Request for Filing and Approval for Reorganization 128

Yesterday, the association submitted a request to the Social Affairs Bureau, saying, "The request is to reply to the order to temporarily suspend activities and to earnestly request the government to comply with the feelings of the overseas Chinese and approve the filing so that it can continue to proceed and reassure the overseas Chinese. We received an order from your bureau, No. She Zi 14181, stating that the association had organized itself without permission from the municipal party department and had not reported to the competent authorities for approval and filing. It had also published advertisements to receive donations before being approved, which is not only prone to abuses but also violates laws and regulations. Now we have received an order from the municipal government, which has been forwarded by the Executive Yuan, to strictly ban it, etc. We have ordered the association to immediately stop activities, separately end them, and report for verification. Do not delay, etc. After receiving the order, we were terrified. The association is organized by more than 800 pure elements of overseas Chinese. Its purpose is to promote mutual assistance, connect the feelings of overseas Chinese, and maintain their interests. There is no other political background. All kinds of facilities have been seen by people in the past year. The Chinese Chamber of Commerce in Surabaya and the Chinese Chamber of Commerce in Vietnam have successively joined as initiating groups. Domestic celebrities such as Xiong Xiling, Xu Shiying, and Wu Ziyu, party and state figures such as Chu Minyi, Luo Wengan, and Chen Gongbo, central committee members such as Zeng Zhongming, Ge Baichuan, Fang Jue, and Wu Xingya, Pan Gongzhan, and other gentlemen from the Shanghai Municipal Party Department Committee are also listed as adults who have participated. It can be seen that the establishment of the association is not only for all our overseas Chinese, but also due to environmental pressure and the needs of the times, and also the same sympathy and request of national leaders. This time, the Executive Yuan suddenly issued a strict order to ban it, which is really unexpected. However, the reasons for the ban are nothing more than the following two points: (1) It was organized without permission from the municipal party department to report to the competent authorities for filing; (2) It also published advertisements to receive donations without reporting for approval. Now the responsible colleagues of the association will make a sincere defense of the above two points and respectfully state them to your bureau first. (1) Our overseas Chinese, in view of the discrimination and abuse suffered by foreigners in recent years, such as the recent anti-Chinese in Mexico and the oppression of Chinese businessmen in Southeast Asia, have been extremely cruel and have never been seen before. The deeper the stimulation, the more the Chinese government is unable to protect it due to environmental relations. For the sake of their own interests, our overseas Chinese compatriots are forced to contact various comrades and initiate the organization of this association in order to concentrate the spirit and strength of all overseas Chinese under the leadership of the government and to precede the self-salvation movement. At the beginning of the initiation (October 7 last year), they had already reported to the local highest party department according to law, requesting permission to establish it. However, the Shanghai Municipal Party Department showed that they were not allowed to do so. They did not know the reason, but they were eager to save themselves and could not give up the public opinion of the majority of overseas Chinese. Therefore, they insisted on the freedom of association and association under the Constitution of the Republic of China and resolutely proceeded with the organization. After the establishment, they again requested filing from the Central Party Department, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, the Shanghai Municipal Government, and the Municipal Party Department on June 5, 6, and 29 of this year, respectively. It is the colleagues of the association who have extremely respected the laws and regulations of the government. The reason why it has not been approved so far seems to be the fault of the association. (2) This time, in the anti-Chinese incident in Mexico, tens of thousands of our overseas Chinese compatriots in Mexico were robbed and massacred, and their situation was extremely tragic. Fortunately, they escaped from the tiger's mouth, escaped into the United States, and were expelled and returned to China. They fled in a hurry, and their food and clothing were cut off. After arriving in Shanghai, they had no home to return to, and various domestic mass organizations and charitable organizations seemed to be indifferent. The anti-Chinese trend in Mexico has lasted for two years, and no one in the motherland has provided relief, which is really heartbreaking. The association is a service organization for overseas Chinese. Seeing the above situation, it is difficult to sit idly by. Moreover, with the masses dying and the opportunity pressing, it is even more impossible to submit a request and wait for approval for a long time before acting. Therefore, in the spirit of sacrificing, rescuing, and helping each other, an emergency donation was initiated, only to be helpful. Since compatriots freely donate private property to save the lives of compatriots, who would worry about the obstruction of the government? Moreover, the donations are entrusted to banks for collection, and the finances can be shown to be open. Therefore, Chairman Chiang and the Central Relief Committee each assisted with huge amounts of money. Even your bureau's fourth second material also repeatedly requested the association to provide relief. The colleagues' initiation of relief for refugees has long been praised by the authorities, and the government leaders have done their best to assist. It does not seem to be a private act. The above two points, right and wrong, are subject to public opinion. The government and the party department both have the absolute responsibility to guide and train the people to organize groups. If it is believed that the association has any improper procedures or measures, it can be corrected by means of orders. If this kind of procedure has not been followed and a strict order to stop it is suddenly issued, or even an order to end it, it does not seem to be the intention to respect public opinion and cultivate mass organizations, and it is far from the government's intention to love and protect overseas Chinese. However, the colleagues of the association have always obeyed the government and supported the party and the country. Now that they have received a clear order to ban it, they should abide by it and immediately suspend all activities, waiting for the government to deal with it fairly and guide its implementation. As for the part of the order to end it separately, the public opinion of all overseas Chinese compatriots is really uneasy. Although the association was established for a short time, it has a considerable understanding in the society, and overseas Chinese all over the world have deep sympathy. If it is suddenly cancelled, not only will all overseas Chinese be greatly disappointed, but also the public will be suspicious of the government's cruelty to overseas Chinese groups. It is a pity that the existence of the association itself is sufficient, and the credibility of our government's three orders and five declarations to love and protect overseas Chinese over the years will be completely lost. As for how to improve the organization of the association and how to make the work legal, it all depends on the government's guidance and promotion or order to reorganize it. The colleagues will definitely follow it unanimously, and strive to make the Global Overseas Chinese General Association legally produced under the principle of practicing the Three People's Principles. Then, tens of millions of overseas Chinese all over the world will definitely praise the benevolence and virtue of our government. We respectfully request your bureau to consider the small labor of overseas Chinese who sacrifice for the country, and immediately find a way to provide relief, and forward it to the municipal government, and submit it to the Executive Yuan for review, and bestow maintenance so that the association can continue to handle overseas Chinese mutual assistance undertakings, so as to comfort the public's hope, and there is no gratitude, and still wait for instructions and orders to comply. Sincerely, Wu, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, Standing Committee Member of the Global Overseas Chinese General Association, Wu Chengyu, Yan Dajue, Chen Daming, Wu Ziyuan Kong Gongwei.
