Chang Chung Officers Establish

Organization for Selling Appointment Letters in Shanghai 133

Four People, Including the Fake Regiment Commander, Adjutant, and Quartermaster, Were Arrested. A Large Number of Seals, Military Uniforms, and Symbols Were Found 丨 The Fake Brigade Commander Zeng Yingliang is Wanted 丨

Recently, a large number of Chang Chung officers have been found in various parts of this port, wearing blue cloth military uniforms, yellow leggings, brand-new leather shoes, carrying armed belts and briefcases, and swaggering through the streets in Caddies. On the left chest is a symbol with a white background and red border (Third Brigade, First Regiment of the Fourteenth Provisional Division of the Army). There are regimental commanders, regimental deputy commanders, adjutants, quartermasters, clerks, etc. They are all the First Regiment of the Fake Brigade Commander Zeng Yingliang.

Issuing Appointment Letters 134

And set up an office in a certain place in the French Concession. Xu Zhiquan, a Taizhou native who used to be a detective in the third team of the first district of the water police force, and others, all requested appointments from He. In addition to paying a considerable amount of cash as a guarantee and a substantial shop guarantee, they must also be introduced by acquaintances. From May 16 of this year, the guarantee money has been successively collected, and the appointment letters have been issued to Deputy Regiment Commander Cao He, Jin Yushan, Adjutant Xu Zhiquan, Sheng Wenhua, Sheng Xu, Zhang Zhiren, Chen Zhengyu, Quartermaster Lu Yinghua, Zhao Zhensheng, Zhang Jun, Service Member Yang Zhiping, Clerk Yan Shouzhang, etc. The military uniforms and armed belts are all handled by He Shaohua on behalf of the applicants. If they travel to and from other places, passports are issued in the name of the Fake Brigade Commander Zeng Yingliang.

Free Rides on Boats and Cars 135

The first regiment commander of the Fake Brigade Command, He Shaohua, carried this passport with him and often traveled between Henan and the Beijing-Shanghai railway line with two orderlies. This matter was learned by the Commander of the Railway Protection Military Police, who immediately ordered Fang Dixia, the first captain of the sixth regiment of the department, to order the railway protection military police under his command to pay close attention and investigate and arrest him. After receiving the order, Fang immediately investigated and found Lu Yinghua, the fake quartermaster, in the first-class car of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway the day before yesterday. He interrogated him, and according to the answer, after being appointed this time, he took the train from Changzhou, carrying 200 yuan, and planned to go to the residence of the regimental commander He Shaohua in the French Concession of Shanghai to pay the guarantee money and find a money shop as a guarantee, and then ask the Minister of Finance.

Minister Song Ziwen 136

To add the appointment, the military police of the team followed Lu Si's car to the North Station in Shanghai, and the fake regimental commander He Shaohua had already arrived at the station to greet him. Therefore, He and Lu, the two criminals, were arrested and taken to the team headquarters for detention and interrogation. Luo Gengtang, a service member of the team headquarters, was also sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau with a document to report to Director Wen Hongen, and was allowed to send personnel to cooperate in the arrest of the fugitive Chang Chung officers, so as to handle the case together. After receiving the report, Director Wen immediately ordered Lu Ying, the captain of the investigation team of the bureau, to send experienced detectives, Gao Juchuan, to conduct a strict investigation as soon as possible. The investigation team found out on the afternoon of the day before yesterday that the fake military agency was set up at No. 107, 4th Floor, Baer Road, the home of the fake regimental commander He Shaohua. He reported to Captain Lu, who immediately sent detectives Shen Jinchu and others to join Chinese and foreign detectives from the French Concession Patrol Room. At about 5 o'clock, they arrested the fake adjutant Xu Zhiquan and the suspect Xie Zhenting. They found an appointment letter book with 26 copies, the official seal of the regimental commander, nine official seals of various kinds, letter paper and letter shells, passport symbols.

Appointment Letter Stub 137

Four blue cloth military uniforms, three military trousers, and overcoats, and several photos taken by fake military officers were taken to the French Patrol Room for detention. Captain Lu personally negotiated with Salih (transliteration), the director of the French Political Department, and reached a compromise. At 12 noon yesterday, the original team of detectives, including Gao, was sent to bring the suspects and evidence back to the team for interrogation. Xu Zhiquan confessed that he was 39 years old, from Taizhou, and lived in Songjiazhai, north of Caojiadu. He had served as a detective in the third team of the first district of the water police force. He was introduced by Yan Shouzhang, the clerk of the regiment headquarters, and received it at 8 pm on the 5th of this month.

Adjutant Appointment Letter 138

One paper, one symbol, until he was arrested, he knew that he had been fooled and asked for leniency. According to Xie Zhenting's confession, he was 39 years old, from Caojiadu. He was arrested at the door for looking for a swallow's nest and did not know anything else. After the interrogation, the two criminals were detained. It is reported that the military police team prepared a document and went to the office to transfer the suspects to Director Wen. Wen would not allow them to be taken back for handling until the official document from the military police regimental commander arrived at the office. The fake brigade commander is now at large and wanted.

After the Huge Amount of Money Was Stolen from the New Ning Shao Company, the Company Strictly Prohibits Private Transportation 139

In order to avoid unfortunate disasters and the lives and property of the entire ship, the case of the New Ning Shao ship of the Ning Shao Company being stolen a huge amount of money has been recorded in this newspaper. Now the continuing news will be recorded as follows.

The Thief Premeditated 140

The occurrence of this case is very strange. The boatman Wei Yuming brought money on behalf of the bank, and even the company did not know about it. The thief disguised himself as a wealthy guest and boarded the New Ning Shao ship in October of last year. After arriving on the ship, he specified that he wanted the No. 12 official cabin and did not allow anyone else to share the room with him. Therefore, he brought an servant with him, and sometimes he voluntarily lived in the room alone and bought two ship tickets so that he could refuse others to share the room with him. He also told Wei Yuming that he liked to go to bed early, and after entering the room alone, he forbade others to make noise there. His deep intentions and secret intentions had already been planned several months ago.

Thoroughly Investigate the Boatman's Behavior 141

After the Kenye Bank reported to the police station, it immediately sent detectives to the Ning Shao Company to investigate Wei Yuming's behavior and the guarantor after boarding the ship. The shipping company told them that Wei was guaranteed by Zhang, the deputy manager of the Minghua Bank, and had always been very reliable. The detectives also went to the guarantor to inquire and also proved that Wei was quite pure and wealthy. This case can prove that there is absolutely no relationship with him. Therefore, the police station only prepared to question the boatman, and the treatment was quite preferential. The boatman's insurance policy stated that fire and theft were not the responsibility, only guaranteeing his escape.

Tracking Down the Thief's Whereabouts 142

The thief's whereabouts are still unknown. According to boatman Wei Yuming, the guest had been on the ship for ten months, and went back and forth about two or three times a month. Each time, for example, for a 6-yuan cabin, the wine money would be given 14 yuan. The person once said that he was familiar with a friend in the Yuchang Coal Company. Now this friend is no longer in Yuchang in Shanghai, but has gone to Hangzhou to do business. Yesterday, it was heard that Shanghai has sent personnel to Hangzhou to inquire about this friend, hoping to investigate the whereabouts of this thief.

The Company Prohibits Bringing Money 143

Yesterday, the company was very angry when it heard about this matter. Because of the recent unrest at sea, the New Ning Shao ship refused to load cash for various banks in order to ensure safe sailing. The boatman secretly collected rewards and transported huge amounts of money on behalf of others, which not only violated the company's regulations, but also was close to stealing water feet. The impact of this was enough to cause greater danger to the ship, which was related to the lives and property of the entire ship. Therefore, yesterday, he specially sent a letter to the ship owner and the first and second mates, saying that the prohibition of boatmen from privately transporting money on behalf of others had been repeatedly warned, but the boatman dared to despise and resist it, which was really hateful. From now on, the ship owner and the first and second mates will be responsible for checking carefully when the ship is opened. If there are any private transportation of large amounts of money and banknotes, in addition to reporting to the company to severely punish the money-transporting person, the money will be immediately returned to the original sender before the ship can be opened. At the same time, a letter was sent to various banks, telling them not to take the risk of entrusting boatmen to transport money, causing other misfortunes. If there are any of the above-mentioned situations in the future, in case of an accident, the money-sending bank must bear full responsibility.

The Shipping Bureau is Not Responsible for Storms and Water Stains on Passenger and Cargo Ships 144

During this hurricane, many merchant ships in Shanghai encountered storms and were in danger, and many suffered losses. However, because they had received warnings from the Observatory in advance, they were able to take precautions in advance. Therefore, no ships were lost. Those who were delayed due to sheltering from the wind will be able to make up for their flights and leave the port one after another until tomorrow. Fortunately, the docks of the China Merchants Bureau took precautions to block the water early, and the passengers and goods in the stacks were not damaged. However, some of the goods stored on the dock were damaged by the high tide because they could not be moved to the stacks in time. The passengers have negotiated with the bureau. Also, the Shunlun ship, which was going to Xiamen, received a warning on the way and immediately sheltered from the wind. As a result, the hull was still hit by the wind and waves, and the 400 pieces of bran loaded on the deck were completely wetted by the sea water and waves, causing huge losses. Because the passengers voluntarily loaded the goods on the deck, the shipping company is not responsible for anything.

The Trunk Corpse Case That Shocked China and Foreign Countries The Two Murderers Will Be Sent to Macau Tomorrow 145

The accomplice admitted that the corpse was loaded and transported to Japan to divert attention. All the evidence and confessions will be ready when they are sent to Macau tomorrow. In the Trunk Corpse Case that occurred on the Shanghai Maru, the murderers have now confessed and the Portuguese Consulate's request for extradition has also been prepared. They will be sent to the Macau court tomorrow for a formal trial. The details of the situation are recorded as follows.

The Accomplice Also Confessed 146

The main murderer, Bartolomeu Remedios, confessed to killing Zhang Cailian without denying it. At first, the accomplice, Joao Remedios, refused to confess to participating in the murder and transporting the corpse to the port. The Consul General used various human witnesses, material evidence, etc. to confront him, and the accomplice, Joao, finally lowered his head and was speechless. He directly admitted that he helped his younger brother put Zhang Cailian's body in a trunk and moved it to the Huishan Wharf and sent it to the Shanghai Maru, hoping to transport it to Japan, shift the attention of this case to other places, and try to cover up the traces of the murder. After the confessions of the two criminals, Dr. Xue Erfo, the Portuguese Consul General, ordered them to be sent to Macau and returned to the formal court for trial.

All Material Evidence Prepared 147

Regarding this case, all material evidence has been completely collected by the Portuguese Consulate. Moreover, regarding the various facts related to proving that the two defendants committed murder and moved the corpse, the testimonies of all witnesses who appeared in court have been recorded by the Consulate, along with the two defendants' confessions of the brutal murder and moving of the corpse, as well as signed statements, etc., all have been collected and are within the case file. It has been sent to the Macau court. The Portuguese Consul has also submitted a complete written report on the entire case from beginning to end, and it will be submitted at the same time when the two defendants are escorted to Macau. Furthermore, a telegram was sent to Macau in advance, reporting that the escort will depart from Shanghai tomorrow.

The Portuguese Consulate will also send a clerk carrying the entire case file and evidence to Macau. The group of convicts and escorts will board a ship tomorrow afternoon, first to Hong Kong and then transfer to Macau. The sensational box corpse case has now come to an end.

Seven Injured in Nanshi Weiwu Branch Road Bombing 149

Nanjing woman Tao Yuzhi suffered the most serious injuries. At the Yongyuan Dyeing and Weaving Factory at No. 20 Weiwu Branch Road, under the jurisdiction of the Second District General Office of the Nanshi Public Security Bureau, the scale is very large and there are many workers. Chen Weigan, a worker from Zhenjiang, 33 years old, hired a rickshaw at 7:15 last night and carried a number of bamboo poles, passing in front of the factory gate. Unexpectedly, just as he reached the Jiadeli intersection, a bomb suddenly exploded by the roadside, with a shattering sound that shook the surrounding area. At that time, Chen, the rickshaw puller, and people at the alley entrance, a total of seven men and women, were injured. Chen himself suffered injuries to his head and legs. Dong Cungen, 32 years old, from Hangzhou, was injured in both legs. Chuan Lianrong, 33 years old, from Hangzhou, who runs a cigarette and paper shop at No. 43 on the road, was injured in his right leg. The child Li Genrong, 8 years old, a local, who lives at No. 43 Jiadeli, was injured in both feet. The woman Chen, 41 years old, from Ningbo, was injured in her left leg. The rickshaw puller Huang Jinfu, 23 years old, from Yancheng, who lives at No. 28 Yuanxingli, Nanshi Wharf, was injured in both legs and abdomen. Su Yulin, 33 years old, from Sichuan, who lives at No. 5 Gongxingfang on the same road, was injured in his buttocks and left foot. The most seriously injured was Tao Yuzhi, a 19-year-old Nanjing woman who runs a boiler shop at No. 19 on the road, who was injured in her left leg. After the incident, the Liyuan Road Police Station under the jurisdiction of the Second District General Office heard the alarm and immediately sent Patrol Officer Li Shoupeng with many police officers to investigate. They saw the injured groaning on the ground and immediately took them to the Shanghai Hospital, and reported to District Chief Li, who reported to the General Bureau for investigation.

Public Works Bureau Begins Collecting New Land Tax After Reassessing Land Values 150

Because land values have increased, an 80% discount is allowed, limited to September 30th for payment. The Public Works Bureau of the Public Concession of Shanghai believes that land values within the concession have increased rapidly in recent years. Therefore, since 1920, a reassessment has been conducted every two to three years. The previous land value assessment was determined in the autumn of 1930 and implemented on New Year's Day 1931. Subsequently, in 1932, the reassessment had already been authorized by the taxpayers, but due to the emergency situation in the area, the Public Works Bureau decided to postpone it to 1933. The new land value assessment was approved in the budget of the current year's taxpayers' meeting and implemented on July 1, 1933. The new land value assessment has long been published in the Public Works Bureau Gazette, and the land tax notices based on the new assessment have also been prepared and will be issued within days. However, the Public Works Bureau is aware that although the new land value assessment is very accurate and fair, there are still many places where the previous assessment was too low, resulting in the new assessment value appearing to be significantly increased. Due to these special circumstances, it has been decided to reduce the increased portion of the land tax payable by registered landowners in the second half of 1933 by 20%, but only if the landowners pay before September 30th. Those who pay after the deadline will still have to pay the full amount. Anyone wishing to apply for a tax reduction can go to the Donations Office at No. 209 Jiangxi Road to obtain a reporting form to fill out.

Ministry of Finance Approves Tax Reduction for Re-exported Used Gunny Sacks by Chamber of Commerce 151

Tax of $0.39 per picul and exemption from surtax. The City Chamber of Commerce previously submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance for an exemption from tax on used sacks, which has been reported in various newspapers. It is now known that the Ministry of Finance has approved the Chamber's request yesterday, approving a tax reduction. The original text is recorded below: "Received and noted. The gunny sack item is listed as a taxable item in both the import and export tariff regulations. The request in the submitted report to use the example of empty containers to exempt used gunny sacks transferred within the customs from transit tax is inconsistent with the provisions of the tariff regulations. However, the statement that the valuation and taxation of used gunny sacks involves cumbersome procedures is indeed true. In order to show compassion for the difficulties of businesses and for the sake of providing relief, all used gunny sacks transferred domestically should be subject to a tax of $0.39 in national currency per picul, and exempt from surtax. This method not only simplifies tax procedures, but compared to the original ad valorem taxation, which totaled $0.90 in national currency per picul, is already a significant reduction. In addition to ordering the Inspector General of Customs to comply, it is hereby approved for notification. This approval."

International Trade Bureau Convenes Fruit Merchants Meeting Again Yesterday 152

Decision to first try selling chestnuts and gingko nuts

The International Trade Bureau of this city, in order to develop foreign trade in Chinese fruits, has repeatedly convened various fruit merchants to discuss ways to open up overseas markets. Since the news was released, it has attracted the attention of British fruit merchants, who have inquired about the details from our consulate in Liverpool. The Trade Bureau convened fruit merchants again yesterday to discuss the methods, which are recorded below:

Discussion Methods 153

The Guidance Department of the International Trade Bureau convened various fruit merchants yesterday to continue discussing methods for promoting overseas trade. Xu Yunqing of Dongshenglong, Cheng Kongshi of Huitai, Zhu Suda of Xie Mao, etc., attended. As a result of the discussion, it was decided to first prepare samples, print promotional materials, and distribute them to various sectors of the country. The goods to be promoted will first be the less perishable gingko nuts and chestnuts, and efforts will be made to sell them on a trial basis. Then, the quantity will be gradually increased and shipped directly overseas for sale.

Difficulties in Promotion 154

According to Mr. Zhang of the Guidance Department of the International Trade Bureau, there are approximately three difficulties in promoting Chinese fruits to foreign countries: (1) The shipping cost is too high. Each box of approximately 60 catties of fruit requires a shipping fee of $7.50, plus a tax of $2, and the extra cost is nearly $10. It is difficult to predict whether the future profits will be able to make up for this amount. (2) The fruits produced in various places this year have suffered from insect pests, and there are very few good ones, making it difficult to compete abroad. (3) Recently, in order to promote domestic products, the Soviet Union has vigorously prohibited the import of foreign goods. Our country exports 10,000 dan of fruit to Russia every year. After this, it will be impossible to sell, which is a major blow to our country's fruit industry.

Award of English and American Reduction Dispute 158

Formally published by the Municipal Government yesterday. The workers of the British American Tobacco Company in this city previously had a dispute due to the employer reducing work, which was mediated by the authorities and was later resolved. However, the employer could not agree on the issue of wages for the period of the slowdown, which led to another slowdown. The Municipal Government submitted it to the arbitration committee for arbitration. On the 5th and 6th, the members unanimously agreed to the following award:

Award of the Shanghai Municipal Labor-Management Arbitration Committee (Disputing Parties): Labor Party: Shanghai Fourth District Cigarette Industry Workers' Union, No. 8 Sanleli, Beikai'er Road, Hongkou; Shanghai Fifth District Cigarette Industry Workers' Union, No. 78 Pudong Ni Du Main Street; Employer: British American Tobacco Company, No. 6 Suzhou Road; The above parties have a dispute due to reduced work. After mediation, the employer did not agree to the labor party's request for wages during the slowdown period, and the mediation failed. The Social Bureau requested the Municipal Government to submit it to arbitration. A special award is made as follows: (Main Text) The request of the workers of the First and Second Factories for wages during the slowdown period, except for the workers of the Second Factory's leaf room who voluntarily slowed down, should be rejected. The remaining workers who were refused work by the factory due to the impact of the slowdown should be paid wages by the factory for the period of work stoppage. The request of the workers of the Third Factory for wages during the slowdown period should be rejected. (Facts and Reasons) The employer has the First (Old Factory) and Second (New Factory) factories in Pudong, and the Third Factory on Taopeng Road in the Concession of this city. In May of this year, the original six days of work per week were reduced to five days, then from five to four days, and then from four to three days. The labor party believed that the workers' wages were calculated by the hour and day, and it was difficult to maintain their livelihood with only three days of work per week. They requested the employer to provide at least four days of work per week, but the employer refused, which led to the dispute. The Third Factory on Taopeng Road started to slow down at 9:00 AM on May 10. In the afternoon of the same day, more than 200 workers from the Third Factory went to the First and Second Factories in Pudong, demanding that the workers of the two factories slow down together. The workers of the Second Factory's leaf room expressed sympathy and slowed down at 7:30 AM on the 11th, and the dispute continued to escalate. Then the employer refused the workers of each factory to work. After the Social Bureau convened a mediation meeting and decided on the number of working days per week, the workers of each factory were able to resume work uniformly on May 18. According to statistics, the First and Second Factories slowed down or stopped work for two days, and the Third Factory slowed down for three days. The committee convened representatives of both labor and management parties for questioning. According to the labor party representative, the reasons for requesting the employer to pay wages during the slowdown period were: (1) The factory reduced work without the approval of the government, so the factory should be responsible for the dispute. (2) The workers' failure to work was either due to the factory's order to stop, or being driven away by the factory, or because the factory was closed and the workers could not enter the factory, so the factory should also be responsible for the work stoppage. (3) Some workers still worked as usual during the above reduced working hours, so they should be paid wages as usual, and although the factory regulations had provisions for shortening working hours, the workers had already expressed disagreement, etc. After consulting the employer's representative, they stated that the labor party's strike was unreasonable and wages could not be paid. The reasons were that the company had reduced work due to the many incidents in North China, reduced orders from various places, and stalled sales, and the losses suffered were greater than those of the labor party. Moreover, the factory regulations formulated by the factory had already been submitted to the Municipal Social Bureau for record, and Article 6 of the regulations stipulated (omitted above) that if the factory shortened working hours, it could also pay wages according to the workers' working hours. The factory could decide to shorten working hours on its own without having to report to the government for approval in advance. Before going through mediation or arbitration procedures, workers who went on strike without authorization violated Article 23 of the Trade Union Law. Disputes between labor and management cannot be declared a strike unless they have gone through mediation and arbitration procedures and have been approved by a secret ballot of more than two-thirds of all members at the members' meeting. Also, in view of the company's consideration for the workers during the workers' past strikes, although it has repeatedly paid wages during the strike period, the results have not won the workers' favor, but have led to the workers' arbitrary strikes. Therefore, strike wages will not be paid this time, etc. After the committee checked the original file of the mediation meeting and reviewed the statements of the representatives of both parties, it recognized that the factory regulations formulated by the employer had been submitted to the Social Bureau for approval and record. Although the labor party had expressed disagreement with the factory regulations, before they had been revised, these factory regulations were effective. The factory had provisions for shortening working hours, and the workers slowed down without authorization because they could not maintain their livelihood with three days of work per week, and their behavior was indeed in conflict with the Trade Union Law. Therefore, the Third Factory's workers' initial voluntary slowdown was not in accordance with the request to pay slowdown wages and should be rejected. The workers of the Second Factory's leaf room supported the Third Factory's voluntary slowdown, causing the dispute to escalate, and the employer did not need to pay wages for the period of slowdown. However, in the First and Second Factories, except for the Second Factory's leaf room, the remaining workers who were refused work by the factory due to the impact of the slowdown should be paid wages by the factory for the period of work stoppage to clarify responsibility. The case was unanimously agreed by all members of the committee and was considered fair. The award is made as in the main text. September, the 22nd year of the Republic of China. Chairman: Luo Panhui, Committee Members: Wang Manyun, Cha Liangjian, Pang Shurong, Lu Keming, Wang Xiaolai.

Chinese and Foreign Relief Society Receives Disaster Reports from Various Places 166

The Chinese and Foreign Relief Society sent Commissioner Zheng Jishoucheng to conduct an on-site investigation of the breach of the Yellow River. The disaster situation in Lanfeng has been reported in yesterday's newspaper. Now, according to the report of the investigation in Kaocheng County, they went to inspect the inside and outside of the city together on the morning of the 4th of this month. The tragic situation was truly unbearable to look at. Only the areas near the city and the city itself were completely submerged. The county office has been moved to Hejiazhuang, about five miles outside the South Gate. The houses washed down by the water accounted for 80% or 90%. The bricks, wood, tiles, and debris still covered the shops in the disaster area. Various items and crushed livestock were also among them. The stench along the way was unbearable to smell. The investigation form attached to the county stated that the Yellow River breached a mouth 170 steps wide from the Xin Nan section, eight miles west of the city. The number of deaths was approximately 30 in the first district and 20 in the second district. The mud was knee-deep, making it difficult to investigate and difficult to obtain an accurate number. More than 3,000 mu of farmland were flooded, and more than 700 head of livestock were drowned. The loss was mainly to the people's food. The area affected by the flood accounted for more than 80% of the first and second districts, with more than 50,000 rooms collapsing. The number of disaster victims was no less than 30,000. The high ground was all sand and mud, and the low-lying areas were still three feet deep in water. Most of the people escaped to the top of the levee, where they were exposed to the wind and ate in the open. Some were also begging in other places, which was truly a great disaster.

It was also reported that the society had recently received reports of typhoon and surge disasters in Chuansha and Baoshan, near Shanghai, which are recorded below: (1) Li, the county magistrate of Chuansha and chairman of the relief association, telegraphed, "Hengsha Island in our county has suffered a typhoon disaster in winter, with fields and houses swept away, and countless deaths. The disaster victims are homeless, without clothes or food, and the situation is extremely tragic and awaits relief. Please provide immediate relief." (2) Jin, the county magistrate of Baoshan, telegraphed, "During the hurricane on the 2nd night, the sea surge washed away 60% of Changxing and other five sands, drowning 50 to 60 sand people. The dikes and seedlings were completely destroyed. Please assist with relief." The society received a flurry of disaster reports from various places, all of which were urgent. Those in charge were distressed by the need for extensive relief efforts, which were difficult to raise funds for. They were pacing around the room, unable to sleep or eat peacefully. They urgently hoped that all sectors would quickly contribute to the cause. Those who wished to donate could send them directly to the society at No. 12 Renji Road.

Jisheng Society Receives Wind and Flood Disaster Reports from Wusong 167

The China Jisheng Society recently received letters from Mr. Gu Danchao of the Wusong Lifesaving Bureau and Mr. Wang Youyi of the Wusong Branch, reporting that Laoshu Sha on the opposite bank of Wusong suffered a tragic hurricane and flood disaster. Customs Proclamation on Inspection and Release Procedures for Nitre and Mineral Products 170

Tang Hai'an, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs and Tax Commissioner Bo Lede, issued Proclamation No. 1317 yesterday, stating the proclamation regarding the inspection and release procedures for nitre and mineral products, in compliance with government orders. Henceforth, the transportation of nitre and mineral products, regardless of quantity, should comply with the Provisional Regulations Governing the Conveyance of Nitre and Minerals and the Regulations Governing Nitre and Mineral Transport Permits of the Ministry of Finance. For transportation within the province, only the Nitre and Mineral Transport Permit with the internal character number of the Ministry of Finance is required for release. For transportation outside the province, the passport of the National Government and the Nitre and Mineral Transport Permit with the external character number of the Ministry of Finance are required for release. All previous regulations regarding nitre and mineral products, where a quantity of two piculs or less may be released at the discretion of the Customs Tax Commissioner if a reliable merchant declares it for industrial or medical purposes, are rendered invalid. All merchants are hereby notified. This proclamation is hereby issued.

Municipal Public Safety and Health Bureaus Instruct Domestic Servants to Pay Attention to Cleanliness 171

The Shanghai Municipal Public Safety and Health Bureaus issued instructions to various domestic servant employment agencies, stating: Regarding compliance matters, it has been found that in the city streets, male and female domestic servants employed by residents often indiscriminately dump garbage and sewage on the streets. Such violations should be punished according to regulations. In order to ensure complete enforcement, the various domestic servant employment agencies are instructed to explain the regulations regarding penalties for damaging the streets in advance to the recommended domestic servants, so as to avoid violations and penalties. If the recommended domestic servants repeatedly violate the regulations, the domestic servant employment agency should also be subject to appropriate punishment. Strict compliance and admonishment are required. This order lists the following violations that will be punished according to regulations: (1) Disposing of animal carcasses such as rats, cats, or dogs on the roads or in the river is prohibited. (2) Damaging garbage bins, toilet facilities, and other public facilities for maintaining cleanliness is prohibited. (3) Dumping garbage in places without garbage bins is prohibited, and dumping outside of the bins is prohibited. (4) Defecating in places without toilets or urinals is prohibited, and defecating in urinals is prohibited. (5) Dumping feces on roads, in rivers, or in ditches is prohibited. (6) Retaining stagnant water containers that are prone to breeding mosquitoes and flies is prohibited. (7) Indiscriminately damaging roads (such as disposing of medicine residue) is prohibited. Violations of any of the above items will be subject to a fine of up to five yuan. If the fine cannot be paid within the prescribed time limit, each yuan will be commuted to one day of detention, with amounts less than one yuan also calculated as one day. (1) When transporting items with offensive odors or easily dispersed materials, airtight containers or appropriate coverings should be used. Violations will be subject to a fine of up to three yuan. If the fine cannot be paid within the prescribed time limit, the above detention provision will apply. (1) Each household is responsible for maintaining cleanliness in front of its door and on adjacent sections of the road. If any damage is observed, it should be promptly dissuaded. If the individual does not listen, the household is responsible for providing the name to the bureau for investigation or reporting to the nearest police officer for prohibition. Otherwise, the householder will be punished upon discovery. Violations will be subject to a fine of up to one yuan. If the fine cannot be paid within the prescribed time limit, the above detention provision will apply.

Chinese Ships Should be Repaired and Manufactured at the Jiangnan Shipbuilding Factory 172

Order from the Executive Yuan

The Jiangnan Shipbuilding Factory is a large-scale shipyard operated by our country that can handle the construction of warships and ships. The Ministry of the Navy, in order to expand the factory's operations and save the state-run shipping industry, has specifically requested the Central Government to order all domestic shipping companies to have Chinese ships built in Chinese factories in order to reclaim lost rights and protect future rights. The original order is copied below. To Whom It May Concern: We have recently received Order No. 4530 from the Ministry of Communications, stating: We have received Secret Order No. 3952 from the Executive Yuan, stating: In response to a report from the Ministry of the Navy, one of the reports humbly requests the Ministry of Communications to issue a circular to domestic shipping companies to have ships repaired and manufactured by the Navy's Jiangnan Shipbuilding Factory in order to reclaim rights. According to the report from the Navy's Jiangnan Shipbuilding Factory, the factory can repair and manufacture ships for shipping companies in addition to naval vessels, in order to assist the development of the domestic shipping industry. Domestic shipbuilding organizations have consistently regarded this factory as the one with the most work. In recent years, foreign-operated shipyards in China have sprung up one after another, seizing opportunities to profit. Not only do foreign ships coming to China favor their own kind and flock to those yards, but the majority of the repair and manufacturing projects for Chinese ships are also contracted out to them. As a result, rights and profits flow outward, and there is no way to stop the leak. This not only greatly harms the country's economy, but also causes China's only shipbuilding organization to be squeezed out by foreigners, leaving it with no opportunity to revive and losing the original intention of saving the country through industry. We humbly request that the Executive Yuan, after carefully considering the situation, approve the request and order the Ministry of Communications to issue a circular to all maritime affairs bureaus, shipping associations, and shipping companies to pay attention to the domestic shipbuilding industry and to have all ship repairs and manufacturing projects contracted to the Jiangnan Shipbuilding Factory in order to reclaim lost rights and promote future industries. The benefits to the future of the Party and the country will be significant. Based on the aforementioned report, the matter should be prepared in writing and submitted for review and implementation, and an order has already been issued to comply. Therefore, an order is hereby issued for the Ministry to relay the order to all shipping companies for compliance. This order is hereby issued, and it is urgently requested that a letter be sent for strict compliance. Hereafter, your company must comply with the order when repairing and manufacturing ships in order to protect domestic rights and interests and respect the orders of the Executive Yuan and the Ministry. With high regards.

The Only Domestic Candy Factory 173

丨Xianghai Confectionery Factory, Large-Scale and Grand丨

Since China's trade with Europe and the United States, the outflow of money each year has been countless. This is because domestic products are often not as refined or well-made as imported goods, and many cannot be manufactured domestically. Therefore, China has become the world's largest importing country. To fundamentally seek a way to resist this, we must pay attention to whether the manufacturing of domestic goods can surpass imported goods, and whether their value is lower than imported goods. If we can achieve good quality and low prices, why would the Chinese people not be happy to use domestic goods? The confectionery industry, although relatively small in the market, has seen a gradual increase in consumers in recent years, and imports of foreign goods have also increased year by year. However, the prices are high, and ordinary people cannot afford to buy them regularly. If one wants to obtain confectionery that surpasses imported goods at a low price, the various products of the Xianghai Confectionery Factory can be considered satisfactory. The factory is a new-style factory completely operated by Chinese merchants, located at 8 Dithmarschen Road in Hongkou. All of the machinery in the factory was custom-made in Germany, and German technicians lead the work. All workers wear white uniforms and gloves, and the premises are very clean, with no mosquitoes or flies. From stirring the sugar to packaging, everything is made entirely by machines, without manual labor. The equipment is thorough, and hygiene is emphasized, which is truly reliable. Furthermore, all of the sugar that needs to be cooked in the factory is cooked by surrounding it with hot air pipes, so the fresh flavor and vitamins of the sugar are completely preserved. Its most famous products are Fanlexiang candy, Fanle toffee, fruit candy, and Wumuya butter candy, etc. The quality is excellent and the taste is delicious. Once tasted, it is felt that it surpasses imported goods in comparison, and it can be called China's most perfect and mechanized confectionery factory. Its products are popular throughout the country and are sufficient to resist foreign goods and stop leaks. We hope that the Chinese people will pay attention to it amidst the calls to promote domestic goods.

Murder Case in a Gutter One and a Half Years Ago Solved 182

The deceased was also a notorious bandit who burned one person to death with kerosene. At around 7 p.m. on February 4 of last year, Sun Yadong, a native of Jiangbei, was assassinated with a knife near a deserted area next to a gutter at the Public Works Bureau Engineering Office near Jingzhou Road and Ningwu Road. The murderer escaped from the scene. Although the police pursued the case, it remained unsolved for a year and a half, and the murderer remained at large. Until the day before yesterday, Shen Yuzhou, a Chinese detective from the Yulin Road Police Station, learned that Zhu Songquan (24 years old), a native of Jiangbei who resided at 588 Yangshupu Road, was involved in the case. He was arrested and sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court yesterday morning. Judge Xiao Fengti interrogated him. Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, stated that the case was reported to the police by Tao Pei, a Westerner from the Public Works Bureau at 267 Jingzhou Road, by telephone at 8 a.m. on February 5 of last year, stating that a male corpse was found near the grassy gutter. The police were dispatched to investigate and found that the clothes worn by the deceased were torn at the shoulders, and the outer pants were stripped off. The underwear was pulled down, exposing the lower body. The head was injured by the gutter. He was sent to the police hospital, where the doctor examined him and found three stab wounds on the head from a metal object. The upper joint of the index finger on the right hand was cut off by a knife. There were also several stab wounds on the middle finger and neck. There was a long knife mark from the right ear to the left ear, which was indeed the fatal wound. Next to the corpse were the upper handle of a pair of pliers and a hemp rope. There were many onlookers at the time, but no one recognized the deceased. When the corpse was taken to the morgue for examination, no family members came to claim it. The reason for the murder was unknown. The defendant admitted to the assassination without denial in the police station yesterday. It is said that he has an older sister named Zhu E'zi, who lived with her husband, Jia Mingsheng, in their hometown of Jiangbei. In November of the 20th year of the Republic of China (1931), a large gang of bandits broke into their home and demanded a large sum of money from Jia. When they failed to obtain the money, they tied Jia up with ropes and poured kerosene on him, burning him alive. His sister witnessed the tragedy and recognized the deceased, Sun Yadong, as one of the bandits. The case was reported to the Rugao County government for the arrest of the murderers. Later, his sister, Zhu E'zi, learned that Sun had fled to Shanghai and followed him. She filed a complaint with the defendant, who, together with his friend Li Zhenghong, agreed at the workshop at 24 Hejian Road that night to have Li's friend, surnamed Zhang, lure Sun Yadong to dinner. When Sun arrived at the place, he saw Zhu E'zi and tried to escape in fear. Li and others chased him with pliers and other weapons to a cement gutter at the Public Works Bureau where water was accumulated. They caught up with Sun, and Li struck Sun's head with the pliers, knocking him to the ground. The defendant was frightened and timid at the time, so he did not know how Sun was killed afterward. However, the cause of the case may have been revenge or jealousy. However, the details still need to be investigated and should be postponed. A photograph of the deceased's injuries taken by the former police station was then presented for inspection. After Judge Fan questioned the defendant for a long time, the testimony of the defendant was the same as that of the police lawyer. He then ordered the defendant to be returned to custody and ordered a change of date to clarify and interrogate again.

Hunan Woman Suicidal Due to Neurasthenia 184

丨Consuming Opium to End Her Life丨

Luo Yang Wenshu, a 32-year-old woman from Hunan residing at 1340 North Sichuan Road, had a husband named Luo Angfu. Last year, her husband received an appointment from a school in Jiangxi and went there to work as a professor. The woman was unwilling to follow him, so she has been living alone in Shanghai for nearly a year. Several months ago, she suddenly suffered from severe neurasthenia and other ailments. Despite seeking treatment from various sources, she saw no improvement. As a result, she became resentful and harbored thoughts of ending her life a few days ago. She secretly consumed opium in an attempt to commit suicide. Subsequently, a maid living in the same residence discovered the situation and immediately reported it to her master, who then sent her to the hospital for treatment. However, the treatment was ineffective, and she soon died. The hospital reported the matter to the Hongkou Police Station, which ordered Detective Xia Shutang to conduct an investigation. Two suicide notes were found in her bedroom, one addressed to her husband and the other to her husband's cousin, Luo Zhuxu. The notes vaguely stated that she had been suffering from illness for nearly half a year without any sign of recovery, leading her to feel that life was meaningless. The detective then transported the body to the forensic examination office on Follen Road. Yesterday morning, Judge Diao Chengtang, dispatched by the First Special District Local Court, arrived at the office to examine the body. During the official hearing, Zhou Picheng, who identified himself as the second landlord of the residence, testified that the deceased had been renting a small room in his house. He stated that his maidservant had noticed her suicide attempt, and he had sent her to the hospital. Luo Zhuxu also provided a statement. Judge Diao concluded that the deceased, Luo Yang Wenshu, had indeed died due to opium poisoning while still alive. The body was handed over to Luo Zhuxu, who signed a statement acknowledging receipt for coffin and burial.

Wife Hangs Herself After Argument with Husband 185

丨Cause Was Watching Mahjong丨

Wang Fangshi, a 21-year-old woman from Changzhou, and her husband, Wang Yunzhang, a salesman for an insurance company, rented a room above the Xiang Taichang Clothing Store at 602 East Youheng Road. The couple had a harmonious relationship. On the evening of the fourth of this month, Wang returned home from work and saw his wife watching others play mahjong in the shared kitchen area. Wang advised his wife not to watch anymore because the players were all men. Wang felt there was nothing inappropriate about it and refused to comply. As a result, the two argued. The day before yesterday, she thought about it and harbored resentment. She had thoughts of ending her life. When her husband was asleep, she hung herself with a cloth belt. When her husband woke up, he found her barely alive and unable to speak. Wang was extremely shocked. He immediately called the neighbors to send her to Shanghai Sanitarium for treatment, but it was ineffective. She soon died. The hospital reported the incident to the Huishan Police Station, which ordered Detective Wang Tongpo to investigate. The body was transported to the forensic examination office on Follen Road. Yesterday morning, Judge Diao Chengtang, dispatched by the First Special District Local Court, arrived at the office to examine the body. During the official hearing, Wang Yunzhang, the husband of the deceased, and Luo Shirong, who lived together, testified to the above facts. Judge Diao concluded that the deceased, Wang Fangshi, had indeed hanged herself while alive. The body was handed over to her husband, Wang Yunzhang, who signed a statement acknowledging receipt for coffin and burial.

Adopted Daughter-in-Law Runs Away, Refuses to Return Home After Being Found 186

Le Wenrong, a 20-year-old young man from Taiping County, Anhui Province, currently residing at No. 2 Dexing Lane, West Xinjiao Street, in the French Concession, works at Dasheng Phonograph Company. In the spring of last year, he met Wang Abao, a 19-year-old daughter of Wang Jifa, the owner of a rickshaw company in Yuchang Lane, No. 36 Kangti Road, who is from Yancheng. The two fell in love shortly after meeting. Le then asked Chen Peizhang, a detective at the current Municipal Public Security Bureau, to act as a matchmaker to communicate with the girl's parents. On March 17th of the lunar calendar that year, the two parties arranged a formal engagement in a room at the Da You Small Inn at the intersection of Edward Road and Zilaihuo Street. At that time, Le entrusted the matchmaker to pay a tea gift of 150 yuan. Wang handed over a lunar calendar birth date report for the girl, which served as a marriage contract. After that, the girl moved in to live together. A wedding ceremony was to be held on a later date. It was, in reality, a modern form of an adopted daughter-in-law. At the beginning of living together, the engaged couple was deeply in love. However, before long, a rift developed. On August 7th, at 9 p.m., A Bao, while her fiancé and his relatives were out, left without saying goodbye. When Le and his mother returned and learned of this, they checked their belongings and found that a small diamond ring worth 131 yuan, a pearl ring, clothes and other items were missing. At that time, they searched everywhere without success and reported the loss to the police station. It was not until the 3rd of this month that Le learned that his fiancée, Wang Abao, had found a new love and was hiding in Lane 5, Yuanli Lane, Xietu Road, in the Chinese area. He reported this to the local Public Security Bureau, who sent police to arrest the girl and bring her back to the bureau. Because the matter involved domestic trivialities, the police ordered the girl to return home with Le to settle the matter. Unexpectedly, when the girl and Le were on Avenue Joffre not far from home, she suddenly refused to go home and argued on the street. The patrolmen saw this and took the girl to the police station. Detective Han Benyong conducted an investigation. Yesterday morning, the girl was sent to the Second Special Court, where Judge Wu Fanglian interrogated her in the eighth criminal court. First, Gu Shuxi, the lawyer for the police station, explained the case and charged her with theft. Then, the plaintiff, Le Wenrong, recounted the situation of his fiancée's escape and presented the lunar calendar birth date report as evidence. Wang Abao claimed that she had been beaten by her fiancé and his relatives and forced into prostitution, so she had no choice but to escape to work in a silk factory in Hangzhou. At that time, she only took her clothes with her and did not take any other items. She also hired a lawyer to defend herself, while the plaintiff also hired a lawyer to file an incidental private prosecution. The court decided that it was necessary to summon additional witnesses and adjourned the hearing to the 11th. The defendant was released on bail of 300 yuan.

Spring and Autumn

Speaking Up for the Flying Cat 201

— Zhan Lu

A strange cat with two wings on its back was discovered in Pingjin, England. It can also try to fly, but it can't spread its wings in the water. It was abandoned on the side of the road, but is now being raised in the Oxford Zoo. The world is truly full of wonders.

Some superstitious people in England are disgusted by this deformed cat. If it cannot be returned to its original owner, it must be killed to eliminate the unusual. I received this news and am very upset for the flying cat. The English hate the flying cat simply because the cat shouldn't have wings, shouldn't try to fly, and the deformed cat must be killed. However, there are many deformed things in the world. Fish can swim and walk, but there are flying fish in the ocean that leap into the air and quickly fall back to the surface. Snakes crawl, but there are flying snakes in the changing part that can flap their wings into the forest and prey on small birds. There are deformed flying fish and flying snakes, but there are not deformed flying cats. In principle, it is difficult to justify.

Since aviation has developed, flying through the air is considered normal. People who can't fly can fly now. Moreover, once the killing starts, they forget humanitarianism. Many air forces on bombers spread poison in the air and are more fierce than winged tigers. They are simply a team of flying Yaksha, wantonly harming the people below. People even want to fly, let alone cats? What's more, although this cat has two wings, it can't fly high?

Cats have the instinct to catch mice, so there should be flying cats. Bats are also called flying mice. They are the dregs of beasts and the spies of birds. They are neither birds nor beasts. If there are no cats to subdue them, then bats will run wild and belong to two countries. Won't they become the bat world? Although cats can catch mice, they cannot catch bats spinning in the air. The cats have to look up stupidly, just like a toad wanting to eat swan meat. I think that the two-winged cat in the Oxford Zoo should not only not be killed, but also be carefully raised to spread its seeds and cultivate its flying ability! If there are flying cats in the world, then the generation of bat comrades who are both teachers and ghosts can be restrained, right? Haha!

The Man on the Road 202

— Yan Qiao

I have never encountered the various ghost tricks that I have seen on paper and heard in my mouth. Although I am not an old Shanghainese, I also know a little about Shanghai's threshold. Who knows that someone came to weigh my weight last night.

I just came out of the Xiaoguanghan listening to drum music. In order to avoid many unexpected troubles, I hired a streetcar even though it was a short distance. Near the intersection of Hankou Road and Shilu Road, suddenly someone shouted behind me:

"Rickshaw puller, slow down!"

The rickshaw puller, whether it was the lesson of experience or because he was chased and caught, really stopped. I thought that I had accidentally torn someone's clothes and had to pay compensation. Who knows that the person who caught up was a black-clad night traveler. I couldn't see his face clearly. Was it ferocious? But the words made people's hearts beat faster. He said:

"Help me."

At that time, I was holding sixteen copper coins, ready to pay for the car. While I kept saying "No", I paid attention to his movements. How ridiculous! (I laughed after thinking about it later, but I couldn't laugh at the time.) His right hand grabbed the rickshaw hood pole, and his left hand reached into his waist to grope. There was no doubt that he was going to show me the pistol that everyone was afraid to see.

I don't know if his art of using an empty city strategy was not skillful enough, or if he saw that I was a poor scholar without blood? He said a slightly tough sentence first:

"Really don't have it?"

Then he said a softening sentence:

"Help me a little!"

At that time, a clever idea came to me. I quickly handed him the car fare and said:

"Take this!"

The following outcome was really unexpected. He contemptuously released his right hand, turned around and left, and muttered in his mouth:

"Who wants copper coins!"

But when I heard this sentence, it was as if I had received the edict of the Emperor: "Forgive you for having no blood. You are unlucky. I hereby proclaim!"

This farce is a new record in my life history. Perhaps the old Shanghainese find it unremarkable, but at least it can be used as a topic for conversation after tea and dinner.

After I finished writing this script, I wanted to write a title. I thought of an old saying in Suzhou, called "There are no gentlemen on the road." It means that when you are extremely bored and walk to the end of the road, there is no gentlemanly style. But I want to praise the man in black, who is a "gentleman on the road."

『Cowherd and Weaver Girl』 Talk by a Scientist 203

— Qing Qu

"Cowherd and Weaver Girl" is a beautiful legend that has been passed down through the generations about two stars meeting once a year. Ancient poets would often sing and write about it, as if they believed it to be a real event. But where did they ever see the "magpies bridging the river"? Alas, if we were to investigate it carefully, we would realize that the so-called "Milky Way" of the past was merely an abstract concept, not based on actual measurements. Therefore, the terms "Cowherd" and "Weaver Girl" came into being. Looking at the "Book of Songs," it says, "In the heavens is the Han River, shining brightly. There is the Weaver Girl, weaving busily all day long." There is only the Weaver Girl, but no Cowherd. Even among the poets, the one who excelled was Chen of the Tang Dynasty. However, his focus was always on the Weaver Girl, and he never mentioned the Cowherd star. It is clear that it was a fabrication, not something they believed to be true. The "Milky Way" is actually a gathering of countless stars, so its volume is extremely small, and its color is very faint. It has many names, such as "stellar gas," "nebula," "star cluster," "star sea," or "star swarm." These are all names for the "Milky Way." If you use the largest telescope to observe it, you can clearly distinguish the "star clusters," but not the "stellar gas." You can also divide it into two hemispheres, northeast and southwest, with a slightly thin and narrow strip in the middle, which can be called the "star belt." In reality, it is the "Milky Way," also known as the "Celestial River," and there is no difference!

Therefore, the story of "Cowherd and Weaver Girl" is very interesting, but when observed through the experiments of scientists, it is debunked. Since the implementation of the new calendar, many women still follow the old customs on the night of the seventh day of the seventh lunar month, reciting, "On this seventh night, look to the clear sky, the Cowherd and Weaver Girl cross the river bridge. Every household begs for skill, threading hundreds of red silks." According to their understanding, they only know about the "Weaver Girl," and the "Cowherd" is left for men to worship. However, after searching through piles of texts, one cannot find anything solely dedicated to praising the "Cowherd." This is truly unfathomable. Could it be an example of the ancient practice of "valuing women and belittling men"?

Brief news: A new Chinese newspaper, "New China Daily," will be launched in Nanjing this month. It is organized by Mr. Zhang Huijian. It is a daily publication with a very novel news format. The supplement section features six serialized novels daily, such as "One Family" by Zhang Henshui and "A Policeman's Diary" by Jin Mancheng, all of which are excellent. The office address is No. 68 Changle Street, Nanjing. Subscriptions are welcome. The cost is one dollar and sixty cents (silver) for four months, including postage (special offer valid for direct subscriptions to the newspaper before the 10th of September). This is a brief introduction as follows.

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 204

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 14: Difficulty in Finding a Spouse, Hesitant and Anxious / Inviting Friends to a Small Gathering, Remembering Past Studies

Just as he was about to serve the rice balls to everyone, Tian Qing waved his hand and said, "We'll get them ourselves, you can go." The waiter left, and Tian Qing brought a bowl of rice balls to Zhao Ziqiang and replied, "Thank you for your trouble. Please send it to Ms. Yang. You must say something polite, not just shove it in front of her without a word." Zhao Ziqiang was, after all, a man, so he couldn't ignore Tian Qing's words. He had to hold the bowl with both hands and brought it to Gui Zhi, saying, "Please have some." Gui Zhi knew that this was making him very difficult, so she immediately stood up. She kept a straight face, neither smiling nor saying anything. Tian Qing laughed and said, "Ms. Yang, that's not right of you. He's being so polite, bringing the rice balls to you. How can you just accept them without saying a word?" Gui Zhi said to Man Ying, "Your Company Commander Tian is always joking. Are you going to do anything about it?" Man Ying laughed and said, "I'm not a soldier, how can he be my company commander?" Gui Zhi didn't say anything more to them, and sat down to eat her rice balls. Tian Qing turned to Zhao Ziqiang and said, "What's wrong? You're done again. Keep talking!" Zhao Ziqiang laughed and said, "I'm not very good at this, and you're still making things difficult for me." When Gui Zhi heard this, her heart stirred. She remembered talking with Ji Zhi here, and he had said something similar. Who would have thought that today, she was going to marry someone named Zhao? Thinking about this, her face turned red as she ate her rice balls without looking up. Everyone assumed that she was shy, a young woman in this kind of place. Zhao Ziqiang's words were already open enough, so they didn't say anything more. Then, Tian Qing smiled at Man Ying, and Zhao Ziqiang also smiled when he saw it. Even when Gui Zhi looked up, she gave a faint smile. (181)

Elegy for My Old Friend Linwu, Four Couplets 205

— New and Old Debris

This morning, I was shocked to hear of the passing of my friend Shanren. I rushed to the Chinese Funeral Home on Ge Road to mourn him. The small room was cramped, and his body lay there. There were no white horses, only green flies attending. Four sentences cannot capture the abrupt separation of man and heaven. I asked his eldest son about his unpublished works, but he replied that he had not had time to organize them due to his illness. The end of a scholar is this desolate. Grieving for the departed, I shall think of myself. Remembering Ziyun, I will collect the scattered remnants and spread them in his place. It is the responsibility of those who live on, and the world has many interpreters. I will not let them be lost and forgotten. My sorrow is not yet exhausted. I present these four couplets, ashamed of my lack of talent, but perhaps they can summarize his life.

First:

Unable to resist the foreign enemy, it is better to die than live? (You said that not resisting Japan is a sign that the hearts of the people are dead.)

Without any attachments, he went to Shanghai alone, forgetting his family for the sake of the country.

Second:

Awake alone and pure, he continued until his death. (After you moved to Shanghai, you did not pursue an official career.)

Both Confucian and Buddhist, his life had a source. (You used spirit writing to conceal yourself and also liked to study Buddhist scriptures and Zen sayings.)

Third:

Children see deep affection, and righteous daughters and sons shed many tears. (You had many adopted children.)

A combination of chivalrous scholar, there is a true evaluation of great scholars and heroes. (You were enthusiastic about justice and loved to help others in the association you belonged to.)

Fourth:

Pure breeze in Shanghai, eradicating corruption and restoring justice with bare hands? (You led the newspaper with verbal attacks and writing, without any scruples.)

His great name stands like Mount Song, his actions fragrant, his aspirations pure, and he has already determined his legacy.

Short story

First Rain (Part 1) 206

— Hu Liwen

Although it is already autumn, the weather is even hotter than summer. Sweat flows incessantly all day long. My mind is somewhat dazed. I want to write a letter home to comfort my mother, but when I hold the pen, I can't write a word. Really, what should I write? It has been several years since I left my hometown. Work has consumed me, leaving me no time to rest, let alone a chance to return home! My mother has written several times to ask about my situation. Of course, I can't tell her the truth, because I'm afraid of hurting her. Although I don't want to lie to her, I have no choice but to do so. In my replies, I always say that everything is fine.

Today, after returning from work, my clothes were soaked with sweat. As usual, I took a bath, changed my clothes, and sat in this wooden box-like room, turned on the electric light, and wanted to read a book. But it felt like an indelible plaster was stuck on my heart. I only read two lines and threw it away. I felt vexed, as if something was gnawing at my heart. I quickly walked to the window, looking at the southern sky, where clusters of catkin-like dark clouds were surging up. Under those dark clouds was my hometown!

Suddenly, a gust of wind brushed my face, and the dark clouds surged up even more, gradually covering the entire sky. The first gust of slanting rain followed, pouring against the window. I quickly closed the window and retreated to the bed. All sorts of thoughts flooded my mind like arrows. I wanted to cry. I covered my face, and tears flowed from between my fingers. The weather seemed to have turned cooler. Raindrops hit the banana leaves and the glass window in the courtyard, making a sound like the rapid beating of war drums. Inside the room, only the electric light blinked, laughing coldly at me. I hated it. I tossed and turned, burying my face in the pillow. I wanted to die, I wanted to commit suicide. I cursed everyone, hated everyone. Their words were all lies. They could buy your body with money, buy your freedom. But I couldn't bear to leave my loving mother, so I was now alive, struggling, even though living had no meaning.

I didn't know when I had returned to my hometown. I stepped into the house and saw my sister cooking in the stove, the smoke filling the room. I forgot that I was carrying a heavy package on my shoulder. I jumped forward and called out, "Sister!" She looked up, saw that it was me, and quickly dropped the thin firewood in her hand, ran over to shake my hand. She smiled and said to me:

"I knew you would definitely come back today, so I cooked many dishes that you like to eat, waiting for you to eat them."

She pointed a finger at the bowls on an old table against the wall and reported to me: Mother is sick, in the room. I followed her to my mother's room. My mother was in bed, her face very pale. This scene filled my heart with half sweetness, half bitterness. I ran to the bed like a madman. I wanted to say something, but there were too many words, and I didn't know where to start. When my mother saw me coming, a mixture of sadness and joy appeared on her troubled face. She reached out and touched my head, saying

"Xiuer, you're back!"

"Yes, I'm back, Mother!"

Mother patted the edge of the bed and told me to sit down. I took off the package on my shoulder, gave it to my sister, and sat on the edge of the bed. My mother held my hand and asked me to tell her about what I was doing outside. I didn't dare to tell the truth. I made up a lie and told her. She shook her head, seemingly unwilling to believe it. Suddenly, tears flowed from her sunken eyes. She choked and said:

"Xiuer, don't lie to me, you've lost weight, you've lost a lot of weight, you must be uncomfortable there?" "No! It's very comfortable there!"

No matter what, I can't tell her, I can only lie to her until the end.

Page 18

Education News

Special Feature: The Children We Need by Pan Gongzhan 207

(Written for the establishment of the Shanghai Children's Welfare Committee)

Amidst the abnormal, excessive, or insufficient treatment of children in China, they have always been regarded as rare toys or unnecessary burdens, unable to obtain the necessary natural development. In all aspects of life, all kinds of evil consequences – weakness, sickness, stupidity, selfishness – are rooted in this period. Because parents use unscientific methods of loving (?), the results are often the opposite of what they expect. We often see that many children in society live in a state of premature aging, losing their lively youthful appearance. This is truly an astonishing and strange phenomenon. No one can deny that the warriors our nation needs now and in the future are strong, brave, intelligent youths who can sacrifice themselves for the public good. Therefore, we must use scientific training methods in children's education to overcome the unscientific love of the past, to maintain the lively and pure spirit of children, and to hone the strong and brave strength of children. All doting on children is a poison that harms children, and it is a poison that harms the nation. Parents and teachers must have a full understanding of this. Today is the day of the establishment of the Shanghai Children's Welfare Committee, so I offer my sentiments to the gentlemen engaged in the children's welfare movement as a reference.

Ministry of Education Promulgates Regulations for Vocational Supplementary Schools 211

The Ministry of Education has formulated regulations for vocational supplementary schools and ordered all provincial and municipal departments and bureaus to comply. The regulations are as follows:

Regulations for Vocational Supplementary Schools

Article 1: Vocational supplementary schools are places for implementing supplementary production education. Their main purposes are as follows: 1. To supplement the knowledge and skills required for their current occupation or to enhance the knowledge and skills of other occupations for those already engaged in work, and to provide them with civic training. 2. To provide vocational knowledge and skills to those who volunteer to engage in occupations, and to provide them with civic training.

Article 2: Provinces, cities, and counties should establish vocational supplementary schools or vocational supplementary classes (hereinafter referred to as vocational supplementary schools) based on local needs (and reward agricultural, industrial, and commercial groups and private individuals for establishing the aforementioned vocational supplementary schools). Schools at all levels may establish them as annexes.

Article 3: The establishment, modification, and suspension of vocational supplementary schools within the administrative region of a province should be submitted to the competent county or city education administrative authority for approval and forwarded to the education department for record. Within the city area directly under the Executive Yuan, it should be submitted to the city education administrative authority for approval and record. Those directly managed by the provincial and city or county education administrative authorities directly under the Executive Yuan should be reported to the higher-level education administrative authority for record.

Article 4: When establishing a vocational supplementary school, the details of the departments to be established, the duration of study, equipment, funding, etc., and the reasons should be submitted to the competent education administrative authority for approval and record.

Article 5: Vocational supplementary schools should submit the roster of faculty and students, academic achievements, income and expenditure, and implementation status to the competent education administrative authority for record at the end of each semester or each subject.

Article 6: The admission qualifications for vocational supplementary schools are that they must have received considerable literacy education and be over eleven years of age.

Article 7: The duration of study in vocational supplementary schools shall be determined by the school in accordance with local conditions and the nature of the occupation, and submitted to the competent education administrative authority for approval.

Article 8: The organization of vocational supplementary schools is divided into the following two types: 1. Semester system: The semester is the unit, and completion of several semesters is the end. The start and end of the aforementioned semester are not restricted by the start and end of the regular school semester. 2. Subject system: The subject is the unit, and completion of a certain subject is the end.

Article 9: Vocational supplementary schools are divided into the following types: 1. Regarding agriculture and sideline industries, such as improved seeds, pest control, fertilizer production, beekeeping, chicken farming, animal husbandry, horticulture, general farming, etc. 2. Regarding industry and crafts, such as electroplating, car driving, car repair, printing, drafting, photography, printing, dyeing, weaving, leather making, etc. 3. Regarding commerce, such as typing, shorthand, bookkeeping, remittance, insurance, advertising, advertising design, etc. 4. Regarding housekeeping, such as cooking, flower making, embroidery, sewing, childcare, barbering, domestic service, etc. 5. Others shall be determined according to local needs.

Article 10: In addition to daily or weekly designated daytime or nighttime part-time classes, vocational supplementary schools may be conducted at any season, winter and summer vacations, spare time, or other specific times, but all must be reported to the competent education administrative authority for approval and record.

Article 11: The establishment of departments and the number of class hours and time per week in vocational supplementary schools shall be determined by the school in accordance with local conditions and occupational nature, and submitted to the competent education administrative authority for approval. The aforementioned number of class hours and time shall not interfere with the work of their current occupation for those already engaged in work.

Article 12: The subjects in vocational supplementary schools are divided into general and vocational subjects. The general subjects shall take civic education as a compulsory subject. The vocational subjects shall include vocational knowledge, skills, and vocational affairs. The content of the aforementioned civic subject may be broader than the civic subject in ordinary schools.

Article 13: Vocational subjects and practical training in vocational supplementary schools shall account for at least 70% of the total, and general subjects shall account for at most 30% of the total.

Article 14: The equipment and funding standards for vocational supplementary schools shall be determined by each province and city with reference to local conditions.

Article 15: Vocational supplementary schools may enroll new students at any time if necessary.

Article 16: Students who have completed their studies in vocational supplementary schools or have completed the required subjects and have passed the school examination shall be given a certificate of academic achievement by the school. Academic achievement shall be calculated by combining examination results and usual performance. Usual performance shall account for two-thirds of the academic achievement, and examination results shall account for one-third. The aforementioned certificate of academic achievement shall indicate the study period and vocational subjects.

Article 17: Public vocational supplementary schools do not charge tuition fees. Private vocational supplementary schools may charge a reasonable amount with the approval of the competent education administrative authority.

Article 18: The provincial, city, and county education administrative authorities shall provide appropriate subsidies to private vocational supplementary schools with excellent performance. Article 19: Vocational supplementary schools shall have a principal or director to manage the school affairs.

Article 20: Principals, directors, or teachers of vocational supplementary schools must have the following qualifications: 1. Graduates of senior or junior vocational schools, specialized schools, or professional schools with more than one year of occupational experience. 2. Skilled craftsmen with general subject teacher qualifications may be handled in accordance with the regulations on teacher qualifications for primary and secondary schools.

Article 21: In addition to the provisions of the preceding article, principals or directors of vocational supplementary schools who have served in major positions in people's organizations or vocational institutions may be appointed.

Article 22: These regulations may be amended by the Ministry of Education when necessary. Article 23: These regulations shall come into effect from the date of promulgation.
