This City's Children's Welfare Association Established Today 212

At 1 PM in the City Government Auditorium

Electing Standing Committee Members and Discussing Association Affairs

The Shanghai Children's Welfare Committee, organized by the four bureaus of social affairs, public security, health, and education of this city, and the Children's Daily News, etc., is the only permanent organization in this city dedicated to the welfare of children. The inaugural meeting will be held at 2 PM today in the City Government Auditorium to elect standing committee members and discuss the association's work plan for the year. The order of the meeting and the list of committee members are listed below.

Order of Establishment 213

(1) Formal ceremony, (2) Election of temporary chairman and secretary, (3) Reporting matters: A) Chairman's report on the significance of organizing this association, (B) Director of the Education Bureau's report on the preparations for this association (C) The chairman will present the constitution of the association (D) The Director of the Education Bureau will report on the association's monthly operating budget (4) Matters for discussion (A) Mutual election of the Standing Committee (B) Provisional regulations for the address of the association (C) Confirmation of Mr. So-and-so as the association's clerk (D) This association's work plan for the year (E) Measures for raising temporary fees in accordance with Article 4 of the association's articles of association.

List of Committee Members 214

The ex-officio members are Mayor Wu Tiecheng,

Director of Education Pan Gongzhan, Director of Social Affairs Wu Xingya, Director of Health Li Ting'an, Director of Public Security Wen Hong'en, and representatives from the City Party Headquarters, Lawyers Association, Physicians Association, City Education Association, Film Industry Association, Daily Newspaper Association, Newspaper Reporters Association, Children's Daily News, Civic Education Center, China Child Welfare Association, and the Book Industry Association. The expert committee members are Qiu Xisheng, Mei Yunying, Liu Wang Liming, Wang Guan, Wang Yiting, Zhu Ziqiao, Zhu Yinjiang, Qin Guanqi, Guo Shun, Du Yuesheng, Chen Bingzhen, Wang Zhongfu, Lu Bohong, Wang Binyan, Chen Heqin, Zhu Shaoping, Hu Xuanming, Hu Shuyi, and Wu Zhihao, Chen Jicheng.

The Association's Business 215

Article 3 of the association's articles of association stipulates the following businesses: (1) Children's Protection Department: Upholding children's rights, reporting cases of child abuse or trafficking, and striving for the liberation of oppressed children. (2) Children's Health Department: Establishing children's clinics, inspecting and guiding the health conditions of children in common families, holding children's health competitions, and investigating the living conditions of child laborers in various factories and businesses, and improving them at any time. (3) Children's Research Department: Measuring and testing children's physiology and psychology, investigating children's character, intelligence, and physical strength, and researching new methods of nurturing and educating children. (4) Children's Business Department: Promoting and inventing various new businesses that are beneficial to children's lives, such as the production or distribution of various items related to clothing, food, housing, transportation, entertainment, and culture.

Citizen Education Center Frugality Campaign 218

Frugality Propaganda Rally to Be Held on the Tenth of This Month

And Preparations for a Frugality Exhibition and Student Talk

Also Cooperating with the Reclamation Bank to Establish a Savings Department

The Shanghai Municipal Public Education Center's central activity for this month is the frugality campaign. It has been decided to hold a frugality campaign propaganda rally on the 10th of this month, and to hold a frugality exhibition and student talk. At the same time, a savings department will be established in cooperation with the Reclamation Bank. The details are as follows:

Propaganda Rally 219

The center is scheduled to hold a frugality campaign propaganda rally at 1:00 PM on the 10th of this month in the auditorium. The order has been determined as follows: (1) Ringing the bell to start the meeting; (2) Singing the Party Song; (3) Bowing to the Party, the National Flag, and the portrait of the Premier; (4) The chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will; (5) Silent tribute; (6) Chairman's report; (7) Admonition from the Municipal Bureau of Education; (8) Speech; (9) Entertainment (including drama, costume performances, harmonica music, etc.); (10) Photography; (11) Adjournment. It is said that the drama "Building a Home with Bare Hands" by Xing Zhong is a self-produced work by the center and is particularly relevant.

Frugality Exhibition 220

In order to promote frugality among the public, the center is preparing a frugality exhibition, with the content divided into three parts: extravagance, frugality, and miserliness. The extravagance section includes dancing, gambling, smoking, drinking, and fancy clothes. The frugality section includes educating children, frugal marriages, patriotic donations, savings for old age, and charitable undertakings. The miserliness section includes not educating children and being unwilling to donate even a penny to save the country. There are also various three-dimensional pictures and model displays, as well as a comparison table of the uses of silver dollars and the proper allocation rate of household living expenses. The collection is very rich. At the same time, the center is also holding a homespun cloth exhibition. The exhibition materials are purely improved products from farmers in the county. The materials are strong and durable, and the colors are new and novel. Introduction coupons are printed and distributed to all sectors. The exhibition will open on the 16th of this month.

Student Talk 221

Student talks are held in stages for students from the out-of-school children's education corps, elementary and advanced public schools, and supplementary schools. The purpose is to instill common sense about frugality, guide students to practice frugality and saving, and cultivate a habit of frugality in order to serve the community.

Establishing a Savings Department 222

In order to facilitate savings for the public nearby, the center has specially joined hands with the Reclamation Bank to establish a savings department, located in exhibition rooms two and eight of the center. The department is divided into children's savings, student savings, women's savings, adult savings, fixed deposit savings, and savings for old age, so that customers can choose at their convenience. The interest rates are favorable and the procedures are simple. In the future, it is also planned to set up a public lending office to help the poor. It is said that the savings department will start providing services as soon as preparations are completed.

Outline of Planned Economics, One of the Shenbao Series, Published 227

Today's world is mired in a precarious economic panic, but only the Soviet Union, which is engaged in a planned economy, stands out and is spared from the disaster. Therefore, the eyes of the Chinese people are increasingly focused on the implementation of planned economics. Shen Zhiyuan collected a variety of materials to write this book, which details its principles. The book is divided into eight chapters, including: The evolution of modern social economy, a comparison of various economic systems, planned economics as a science, the essence, prerequisites, and regularity of planned economics, the internal contradictions of socialist planned economics, the Soviet Union's planned economy, the circulation of commodities, currency turnover, and credit under the planned economy, and the issues of profit and capital accumulation in the planned economy. Fu Xiangming recommends it as essential reading for studying economics. The actual price is 3.5 yuan. During the special autumn school opening month, a 30% discount is offered for the purchase of ten or more copies.

Free Talk

From Deafness to Muteness 243

— Luo Wen

Doctors tell us that many mutes are not actually unable to speak with their throats and tongues. It's just that they've been deaf since childhood, unable to hear adults speaking, with nothing to imitate. They assume that everyone else is just opening their mouths and making meaningless noises, so naturally, they can only do the same. Therefore, when Georg Brandes lamented the decline of Danish literature, he said: Literary creation is almost completely dead. No matter what kind of human or social issues arise, they fail to evoke any interest, or, aside from newspapers and magazines, they never stir up any debate. We see no strong, original creations. Moreover, there is now almost absolute disregard for absorbing the spiritual life of foreign countries. Thus, spiritual 'deafness' inevitably leads to 'muteness.' (Preface to the first volume of "Main Currents in Nineteenth-Century Literature")

These words can also be applied to critique China's literary and artistic circles. This phenomenon cannot be entirely blamed on the oppression of the oppressors. The enlightenment thinkers of the May Fourth Movement and their subsequent opponents should both share the responsibility. The former were too eager for quick results and did not translate many valuable books. The latter deliberately vented their anger, even scolding translators as matchmakers. Some young people added fuel to the fire, and for a time, even including the original text when annotating names of people and places for readers' reference was denounced as "pedantry."

What is the situation now? Bookstores with three-bay storefronts are not uncommon on the Fourth Road, but the shelves are full of thin booklets. To find a large volume is as difficult as sifting gold from sand. Of course, being tall and fat doesn't make one a great man, and producing a lot and in great detail doesn't necessarily make one a masterpiece, especially with "cut-and-paste" work. However, a small "What ABC" booklet can never encompass all academic and artistic knowledge. A stream of turbid water is not as clean and clear as a glass of pure water, but distilling a portion of the turbid stream can yield many glasses of pure water.

Due to years of selling empty promises, the literary world has become desolate. Although the form of writing has become relatively more polished, the fighting spirit has declined rather than advanced. Writers become famous quickly through bought titles or mutual praise, but because of vigorous puffery, the shell becomes larger, while the inside appears even more hollow. Consequently, they mistake this emptiness for loneliness, seriously telling it to the readers. Some even go so far as to display the decay of their hearts as a kind of inner treasure. Essays are considered successful in the literary garden, but even the top three selections of this year's anthologies give one the feeling of "the sable coat is insufficient, so a dog's tail is used to continue it." Using chaff to feed the youth will never make them strong. Future achievements will be even smaller, resembling the "last man" described by Nietzsche.

But introducing foreign intellectual currents, translating world masterpieces, all the routes for transporting spiritual food, are now almost blocked by the manufacturers of deafness and muteness. Even foreign lackeys and rich young masters will sneer at it. They want to cover the ears of the youth, causing them to become deaf and mute, withered and small, becoming the "last man." They will not rest until everyone can only watch the erotic pictures sold by rich men's sons and mistresses. The struggle of authors and translators who are willing to be like soil has reached a point where it cannot be delayed. This means striving to transport some real spiritual food and placing it around the youth, while sending those manufacturers of deafness and muteness back to the dark caves and mansions.

The Sorrow of the Literati 244

— Huo Yun

Reading the local news in the Shen Bao of the sixth, I learned that the young writer

was liberated, and fortunately, he did not die under the knife or in a ditch, but rather "died peacefully in his sleep" at the Red Cross Hospital, which is considered "a blessing from heaven." Therefore, we don't need to feel sad or mourn for him.

I had known him for less than half a year. Every time I saw him, I always felt that his "face was pale," which proves that he was in a state of semi-starvation for a long time. I heard that he had been in prison and suffered torture. Life was like a sharp knife, cutting him apart inch by inch, and like a heavy rock, pressing him down firmly. However, he never succumbed to life or assimilated to the environment. He would rather chew coarse bread than chew on his own integrity, and would rather starve to death than sell himself piecemeal. Every time I saw him, his seemingly weary but very resolute spirit always made me feel awe-struck. In this era, he was unfortunate enough to be born without the innate ability to be a "dog." His suffering from cold and hunger, and even going to prison and being tortured, was perhaps "deserved." However, this is precisely what makes Peng Konghuang memorable to me.

He died in a third-class ward of the Red Cross Hospital. Of course, his death was partly due to illness, but also partly due to poverty. After his death, he left behind a widow and orphans. The deceased could not be buried, and the living could not live. A writer who strives to transform society receives such a cold reward from society. I think this is truly the sorrow of the literati.

At this point, I think that some of the writers who truly make a living by selling their writing rather than selling their integrity should, regardless of their literary and artistic affiliations, sincerely organize themselves and, starting from the great sympathy of mankind, engage in mutual assistance in life. When something like Peng's death occurs, where the deceased cannot be buried and the surviving family cannot live, they can use this kind of mutual assistance to settle the matter.

But this may just be my personal ideal, because on the current Chinese literary scene, a live drama of "people eating people" is流行(popular), and "mutual assistance" will certainly be regarded as "theory of pedantic scholars."

Night at the Beach (Continued) 245

— Bing Xin

"No, we must go forward, all the way to where there are lights." Chen said resolutely.

"There are too many rocks ahead, and the ground is wet, making it difficult to walk. Anyway, it's the beach, so it's the same as here."

"No! We don't care about the rocks or the wetness. In short, we must go forward and walk to where there are lights."

"Lights? It's just a small boat traveling on the sea. Look, the more we go forward, the farther it gets away from us. If we chase it like this, I'm afraid we won't catch up with it until dawn."

It was Xin's discovery that reconciled the conflict between the two. Not far from the swimming pool, the three sat down together. The fine sand was so soft and lovely, like sitting on a velvet carpet. The coolness that penetrated to the bones was like entering a crystal palace. Xin and Chen both lay down, but Zhu was still sitting. She was an older sister, afraid of getting her clothes dirty or the dampness affecting her, causing her back pain, so she wouldn't lie down no matter what.

There was no sound. They were now each enjoying their own happiness, each imagining their own future.

"If I have a chance to build a small house by the sea, every night I would come out for a walk with two or three friends, watching the moonlight and the sea embrace, listening to the whispers of the tide and the gentle breeze. In the morning, I would absorb the fresh air by the sea and watch the beautiful sunrise. During the day, when others are dying from the heat, I would open the windows on all sides and let the cool sea breeze blow in to let me read. When tired, I would let the god of sleep take me to sweet dreams... I don't need anything else, just a chance to live this kind of life for a while, and my life will be happy!"

This was Zhu's hope.

"Let me lie here quietly, don't wake me up, let me enjoy the natural beauty like tonight forever. This beautiful moon, the magnificent sound of the waves, the great sea has melted my soul. I have no dreams, I only wish I could lie here forever like this, with the moon, the sea, and the wind never leaving me."

Chen was scientific, but at this moment, he completely forgot his interests. All that existed in his mind was the goal of enjoying the natural beauty as much as possible. He wanted to grasp this moment tightly, he wished the night, this beautiful night would never disappear forever. Only Xin, this poor child, was indeed too bitter. On the one hand, she compared the tide to the times, saying that the angry tide of revolution was like the sea, and no one wanted to resist it when the tide came. It could sweep away all obstacles, wash away all dirt, and destroy all solid dikes. She loved the sea because of its greatness, the magnificence of the seawater. She believed that every sound of the waves colliding was the power of life, not only the sea's, but also people's life force. She wanted to throw herself into the revolutionary furnace, sacrifice herself in the pool of bright red blood; but on the other hand, she loved the silence of the sea, the tenderness of the sea, and the beauty of the green seawater. She wished to walk slowly into the sea under the dim moonlight, letting the magnificent waves play a dirge, and the gentle sea breeze gently caress her corpse floating on the blue waves. The Moon Sister and the stars would emit compassionate light to mourn her. In this way, quietly, without anyone knowing, except for the moon, starlight, wind, and sea, she left this troubled world and realized the ideal of "I don't want anyone to see my corpse."

The night deepened, and the sound of the wind gradually became sharp. The sound of the waves became even louder, and the tide had risen to the feet of where they were lying. Xin really wanted to put her ideals into practice, but there were still two people next to her hindering her.

Because of Zhu's urging, they reluctantly said goodbye to the sea and lazily stepped onto the lonely road home in the moonlight.

Random Notes on Mountain Living 246

— A Ying

(4) Banning Su Dongpo's Writings

Su Dongpo's writings were once banned, which is truly astonishing to modern people. I saw a record of "Banning Su Dongpo's Writings" in Fei Buzhi's "Liangxi Random Notes," Volume 7, which said:

During the Xuanhe period (Song dynasty), the ban on Su Dongpo's writings was very strict. A scholar secretly carried Dongpo's collected works out of the city, but was caught by the gatekeeper and sent to the authorities. Seeing a poem at the end of the collection, it said:

Where the literary star falls, heaven and earth weep,

This old man is dead, and my path is exhausted.

His talent far surpassed that of Sheng Zhongda,

But even in death, his fame is still feared by Yao Chong.

The human world feels devoid of purity,

Has the country ever recognized the ancient style?

Who cherished ten thousand pieces in his lifetime?

The Six Ding (Taoist deities) collect them and send them to the Jade Palace.

The magistrate, admiring his character and fearing implication, secretly let him go.

The misfortune of Su Dongpo's writings can be seen from this small note. At the same time, it can be remembered that no matter how you ban it, those who need it will always need it. Qin Shi Huang was the most thorough, he simply started with the "scholars" who could write books, "burning books" and "burying scholars alive." What was the result?

Books exist, and scholars have not been "extinct." Those who need them will have their own methods of obtaining and printing them. "Very strict" is useless. If everyone does not need it, even if the powerful give all kinds of assistance, there will be no slightest push. Overthrow the enemy and support oneself. If this "oneself" is "deeply hated and loathed" by everyone, assistance will not be able to support it.

Correction 247

In the article "Criticism" and "Humor" besides the one on the fifth of this kan, in the twenty-ninth line, the word Expressionl was incorrectly written as Explanation, which is hereby corrected.

Woman (15) 248

— Shen Congwen

A car stopped on the land in front of the XX Hotel in Xishan. A man came out, a handsome and beautiful man, and a woman, a woman in a green silk gown. The two looked at a bright room on the third floor. After a while, the luggage on the car, a yellow box, a small black typewriter box, was moved from downstairs. The woman told the uniformed servant and told the driver to wait for an hour before going down the mountain.

An hour later, when the car was running towards the city on the flat official road of Bali Zhuang, it was just an empty car.

Near dusk, the man, wearing a thin woolen coat, stood with the woman on the stone railing of the hotel roof, looking at a wisp of haze flowing between the flat fields and distant villages under the mountain. There were clouds in the sky like a woman's cheeks, and a star appeared in the northeast corner of the sky. Everything was like a dream. In front of the hotel was the avenue leading to the Upper Eight Great Sites. On the mountain road, there were two schoolgirls wearing middle school uniforms and a man in a turn-down collar shirt and yellow shorts, asking the hotel doorman for directions to a certain place on the mountain. At a glance, you could tell that these young people were traveling together from the city.

The woman looked at the man beside her, who had just recovered from a long illness, and sighed softly.

About half a mile from the hotel, there was a small mound, planted entirely with black locust trees. The woods were bathed in the setting sun, and the yellow leaves felt even more dazzling. The man seemed interested in the small mound and said to the woman:

"Shall we go over there and take a look?"

The woman glanced at his face and said softly:

"Shouldn't you be resting?"

"I like that little mountain." The man said, "It seems like this mountain belongs to us."

"You can't get too tired!" Although the woman said that, she turned aside to let the man go first. "I feel great, let's go have some fun, and we'll have a good meal when we come back."

The two soon arrived at the woods on the mound. Everything here was exactly the same as the seaside place three years ago. When the two walked into the woods, they were both surprised and walked quickly through the woods as if at the end of the woods was the vast sea that changes without end. But when they reached the end of the woods, they realized that there was no sea in front of them, but just a private cemetery. The woman was stunned when she saw the cemetery and stood there in a daze. The man didn't notice the cemetery, but smiled happily, because further away, the setting sun gilded everything on the earth, and the extraordinary scenery in front of him was indescribably magnificent.

The man seemed to have walked a little too quickly and was panting slightly. After handing his hand to the woman, he asked the woman if this place was like a place that the two were very familiar with. When she heard this question, she sighed slightly, smiled reluctantly, and used this smile to conceal her emotions.

"Memories make people younger." The man said to himself.

But the woman answered in her heart: "When a person lives on memories, it shows that all that is left of this person's life are just some residual dregs.

The evening breeze gently brushed the locust trees, and yellow leaves fell on the two people and around their feet. The man was very happy in his heart and deliberately said in a sentimental way:

"Summer is over, spring is ahead of summer, and autumn comes after summer. What a beautiful autumn!"

As he spoke, he looked at the woman's eyes, eyebrows, mouth, and nose, which had an autumnal feel. She was indeed beautiful, but at a glance, you could tell that this beauty was not the flourishing flowers of March, but the yellow leaves of August. But now he felt that she was particularly lovely, and he felt that that touch of charm made her transcend the limitations of time and become eternally innocent and lovely, and eternally moving and absorbing. He thought of the relationship between the two over the years, how it was intertwined with tears and smiles. He thought of the things that happened to her because she loved him, and he thought of himself, how he had been loved over the years, but at first glance, it seemed that he was deliberately avoiding it, but in fact, it was just an irrational rejection. He felt a bit ashamed, stretched out a hand to the woman, and when the two held hands and looked into each other's eyes, he said softly apologetically:

Discussions

On Modern Literary and Artistic Trends 275

"Literature for life" and "Literature for art" are two major issues in modern literary and artistic trends. However, I believe that whether it is "for life" or "for art", all works must have vitality. Strong "vitality" is the activity of human "desires", and "competing desires" is the main element of artistic action. "Appetite" and "sexual desire" are the main elements for maintaining and releasing survival. Although humans have emotions, they cannot ignore food and reproduction and only talk about "aesthetic desire" or exclusively pursue artistic activities and create "literature for art." But neither can they be like animals, only pursuing reproduction and lacking emotional pursuit of beauty, and only talk about trivialities in life and create "literature for life." In fact, "literature for life" and "literature for art" are already forced terms. Life should have artistic impulses, if we do not ignore "aesthetic desire," one of the three major desires. From a broad perspective, "literature for life" can still be an acceptable term, because literature portrays life, and life is multifaceted (not only focusing on aesthetic emotions, but also taking into account eating and mating). Therefore, all literary works should have the vitality to express various human desires. This is just my opinion, and it is essential. As for the "ivory tower," "struggle in life," and other ideological claims, they should be interpreted separately, because they are related to social evolution and class changes.

I do not approve of those who live leisurely in an "ivory tower," but neither do I approve of "proletarian" individuals who shout empty slogans!

The proletariat can create genuine works of art that reflect their true lives to the world. But now, all we see are unrealistic and alienating slogans with propaganda. Similarly, right-wing writers only want to escape reality. However, this is a necessary phenomenon in today's chaotic society, a transitional stage. If left-wing writers embark on the right track, true works of art may emerge. However, we should be a little indifferent and not fall for these two kinds of tricks in the chaos. We cannot simply write about beautiful scenery, nor can we blindly deceive illiterate workers. Therefore, before we fully understand everything, we should adopt a "general" attitude to research and observe.

"The Accusations Were Found to Be Without Factual Basis" 276

— Shi Ben

A Dark Scene of Society

"A Three-Year Village Head is as Poisonous as a Snake" 丨 The common people's fear of the village head is like that of snakes and scorpions, which has been fully exposed in this common saying. This is nothing more than a legacy of the poor social system in China! None of the village heads do not take advantage of their power to bully the people and exploit the villages. The ignorant and uneducated, pitiful common people are at the mercy of these fellows. They swallow their anger, dare to be angry but dare not speak out! Not to mention the word "resistance." Since the flag of the blue sky and white sun was raised high on the pole, all feudal titles in society were sent to their final rest and eliminated. The word "village head" was, of course, no exception, transforming into a "tax collector." But their [village heads] acts of taking advantage of their power to bully the people and exploit the villages have not disappeared due to the change of name! Village head, tax collector, is nothing more than a set of "changing the soup but not the medicine," a ridiculous trick.

Wang XX, the tax collector in X village, arrogantly relied on the power of the government to bully the ignorant people in the village, threatening them with benefits and instigating lawsuits, leaving the people in X village devastated and full of complaints! At that time, some slightly knowledgeable people felt the pain of being trampled by Tax Collector Wang to the extreme. His means of destruction and coercion were also extremely cruel. How could they continue to swallow their anger and endure injustice? Therefore, they jointly gathered more than twenty villagers and wrote an indictment listing Wang's great crimes of violating the law and harming the people, and went to the government to accuse him. But after the indictment entered the government office, their [villagers'] hearts became uneasy again, and their faces fully revealed their fear. It turned out that Tax Collector Wang had strong backing and great power. For the common people to sue him was like striking a stone with an egg! Lest "drawing a tiger but failing to resemble it and instead resembling a dog" resulted in "stirring up a hornet's nest," wouldn't that be inviting disaster upon themselves! After everyone thought it over, they all felt fearful and regretful for going to sue Tax Collector Wang.

Tax Collector Wang learned that the people of his jurisdiction were suing him and immediately ran to tell his only backing, Gentleman X.

Gentleman X said to him: "You don't need to panic. See what the wind is blowing." In Gentleman X's experienced tone, Tax Collector Wang's courage suddenly increased! A heart of "a guilty conscience" was greatly comforted.

This was probably the effect of Gentleman X's magical power. After the government received the people's indictment, it did not issue a summons to gather the defendant for trial, but casually sent the original indictment to Li XX, a county official who had been waiting for a position in the county government for a long time, for secret investigation and reply. Li XX understood that this was because the county magistrate remembered that he had been waiting for a position for a long time and was extremely panicked due to economic hardship, so he specially gave him a "profitable" matter to handle.

When Committee Member Li arrived at X Village, the first visiting card was sent to Gentleman X's residence.

It is said that Gentleman X hosted a dinner tonight, inviting Committee Member Li XX of the county government. When Committee Member Li was drunk and got up to bid farewell to Gentleman X, the air in Gentleman X's reception room suddenly became tense! The gas lamp hanging overhead also suddenly changed, and the pure white and dazzling light suddenly transformed into a dark and blurred light. At this time, on the large table in the room, there seemed to be two mysterious items arranged, one like a bank check, and also like a government document; and a stack of things like a prescription after being cured of illness, and also like banknotes that everyone loves. Beside them, two people were whispering to each other in private, their faces blurred, looking three parts like Gentleman X and Committee Member Li!

X days later, a piece of news was published in the X County People's Daily: "(X Village citizens XXX, etc., jointly sued X Tu tax collector Wang XX for violating the law and harming the people. After being secretly investigated by Li XX, who was appointed by the county government committee, it was reported that 'the accusations were found to be without factual basis.' Therefore, the county government has dismissed the lawsuit filed by the citizens, etc."

On Filial Piety 277

— Lie Huo

A few days ago, I discussed "rites." Now I am going to discuss "filial piety." It is not because I maliciously want to settle accounts with the Chinese people, but because I am unaccustomed to the fact that the old etiquette and teachings are collapsing, and there is no way to construct new ones during the current transitional period. The smoky atmosphere of "filial piety" is equally intolerable and equally in need of liquidation.

Needless to say, "filial piety" is another kind of national essence with rich color and fragrance. Since Zeng Shen, for thousands of years, it has been deeply engraved in the minds of the general public, and it has become the first step in "cultivating oneself." Because of this, it has the most powerful influence on human life. Nowadays, the old-fashioned people are still worshiping and prostrating, and even the fashionable figures in ties and suits, who are full of foreign air, are also trying to "be hygienic"? It's just that when they are down and out, they all like to talk coolly, and even go the way of "despising" it. However, once the bad luck is gone and good luck comes, and they are commanded by Macmac, they will also "have inexhaustible filial piety" (?). This is often done more on the outside and is most hypocritical on the inside.

Let's see what kind of filial piety is practiced by the general public now?

When parents are alive, the most common kind of "filial piety" is the provision of the mouth and body, which means that they should be served very thoughtfully in terms of material enjoyment. For example, in Shanghai, which lives in a temperate zone, there are no fresh vegetables in winter, so you may want to take a boat or car to the tropics to buy some back (you can also ask someone to bring them), roast them well, and offer them to the table of your strict father and loving mother, and respectfully persuade them to eat. This is "filial piety," and this will "spread your reputation, and everyone will admire it."

Secondly, the words and deeds of the strict father and loving mother, even if they are ugly to the point of stealing and selling prostitution, or like the current trend of being a traitor and selling out the motherland, should be followed only by the parents' orders, without adding any criticism, and the same filial piety can also win a "filial son" from the social people.

Naturally, these are still small aspects of "filial piety." The most important thing is to be filial to the point of "making a name and honoring parents" in the Three Character Classic. To "make a name" and "honor" them, you must abandon the "farming" and "business" and become the only [page break]

Page 22

To the esteemed readers: This company exclusively manages Zhenhua Yonggu Paint Company's Flying Boat brand of various thick paints, magnetic paints, bright black paints, and improved gold paints. In order to expand, the prices are particularly restrained, the quality is particularly excellent, and the delivery is particularly fast. We have selected the 7th and 9th of this month to move to 53 Bailu Lane, Broadway Road, to continue business as usual. We would be grateful for your patronage (telephone 42895) 4373. Special Announcement. "scholars." In the past, in China, all scholars had some hope of becoming officials. Even if they couldn't, they might as well spend some money to "bribe" and "buy" their way in. Once they became officials, their reputation would surely spread far and wide, and their parents would be greatly honored. They had to bring out their strict father and loving mother anytime and anywhere, and call them "old lady" and "old master." This is said to be the most effective kind of "filial piety." Those who can do this are naturally the most outstanding "filial sons."

If, by chance, "Yaochi" urges and the parents suddenly pass away and ascend to immortality, then it is necessary to widely issue "obituaries" and "biographies," and it is also necessary to ask celebrities to write praises, and all of them must write "beautiful words." And they must be "deeply sinful." When writing the biography, they must be "incoherent." The female juniors, when handling the funeral, when the ritual officer shouts "begin mourning," they must "cry loudly," like playing mournful music, wave after wave. This is considered "sacrificing with etiquette." Then they need to "be in mourning for three years," and the masters have regulations that they cannot engage in wedding or other happy events. In this way, those who sleep underground will also praise the filial piety of their grandchildren.

We see, these, these, are how much pretense, hypocrisy, how much irrelevance to life, and how much defilement of the essence of "filial piety"! Just look at the disputes over inheritance, which often occur when the parents have just passed away, and then make a big fuss in court, and you can deduce it from this.

But we do not oppose "filial piety," but our understanding of "filial piety" is somewhat different. True "filial piety" and "filial sons" should be like this:

(1) In their youth, they should inherit and learn from their parents' good education and good life, and not play and be prodigal, so as to worry their parents.

(2) After adulthood, they should seek self-sufficiency and economic independence, and not rely on their parents' old-age property, and be a human being in society.

They should work hard in their careers, serve society, and seek welfare for the masses, so as to fulfill the meaning of life and repay their parents' hard work, and not do evil to society and cause harm to the human masses.

Dreaming of an Ancient Kingdom 279

— Hou Ying

In a trance, suddenly an ancient city appeared before my eyes. The broad and long city walls, majestic and dangerous, also contained some magnificence. Although it was very far away, it already felt as tall as a small mountain. The tricolor national flag reflected the bright sunshine, fluttering in the wind above. There was no one with the slightest vitality, and the numb expression was like a living corpse. Their bodies were as weak as wax; their eyes were as small as beans; their will was as thin as paper; their blood was as cold as water; their spirits were as withered as grass. Alas! In the world, there is a nation that is still dreaming and has not awakened!

Suddenly, a team of soldiers came towards me. Their yellow military uniforms shone in the sunlight like a ball of fire. This ball of fire scorched the weak people, and they all retreated to both sides. I suspected that they were another nation. Sure enough, I recognized their sharp voices as the beasts on the jagged peaks outside the city. It was pitiful that the creatures in this ancient kingdom were drunk and dreaming, and they would all be swallowed alive one by one by this group of beasts! They carried guns with bayonets, proudly striding in neat steps. The snow-white bayonets still had traces of red blood on them. Under the loud abdominal sounds, I heard the groans of the nation in this ancient kingdom. They were like a scorching sun, making people afraid to look directly at them. They used the tips of their guns to drive the people in this ancient kingdom like people driving cattle and horses. They were simply the . . . . Dozens of withered corpses were hanging on the streets, and many compatriots were gathered below, gesticulating and praising! The conscience of this nation has been lost to such an extent that I feel sorrow and shame for them!

After walking past the branch, a big river lay across my path. On both sides of the river, there were many reeds growing, and the autumn wind blew, and they all fell with the wind. The river water was unusually turbid and stagnant, just like this lifeless nation. When I went closer, I found that it was blocked by a large amount of soot.

My heart was茫茫然 and it seemed like I had some feelings. I walked and didn't know how far I had gone. Suddenly, the sound of killing and fighting was transmitted to my ears by the gentle breeze. I raised my head and looked carefully and unexpectedly found that it was the same nation that was cruelly killing each other; then I saw the beasts on the jagged peaks laughing loudly! I sighed and turned around and walked out of the open city gate with no one guarding it. The remaining rays of the setting sun were shooting through the treetops, illuminating the mottled city walls, as if they were sighing and shedding tears there! At this time, something seemed to be getting more lively and energetic. I slowly took a step and walked forward, gradually realizing that there were many peaks hidden in the clouds and mist around the ancient city, and from time to time there were sharp roars coming from those peaks, and I knew that there were unusual beasts. I went forward again and saw the ancient city bricks, piled up with mottled spots, as if to indicate that it had supported a long history of four or five thousand years in this den of tigers and wolves; I naturally had respect in my heart for this great ancient country; although the open city gate without a single city guard made me a little surprised, it did not diminish my respect at all.

The city was very calm, so calm that it was beyond my expectations. The weeds that were taller than my head spread all over the land, and the moss at the foot of the wall was telling of its loneliness; I quietly walked forward alone, parting the thorny grass and humming a song in a low voice; "Could this be the second Babylon? Otherwise, why is it so desolate!"

After a while, I finally walked to a place with human habitation. However, the people were also strange. Whether they were working, talking, or walking, they were all very desolate; I looked around and felt that they were so contaminated that the essence of 'filial piety' was being struck. As long as you look at the disputes over inheritance, which often occur at the new death of the parents, and then make a big fuss in the court, you can extend it to him.

But we do not oppose "filial piety," but our understanding of "filial piety" is somewhat different. True "filial piety" and "filial sons" should be like this:

(1) In their youth, they should inherit and learn from their parents' good education and good life, and not play and be prodigal, so as to worry their parents.

(2) After adulthood, they should seek self-sufficiency and economic independence, and not rely on their parents' old-age property, and be a human being in society.

They should work hard in their careers, serve society, and seek welfare for the masses, so as to fulfill the meaning of life and repay their parents' hard work, and not do evil to society and cause harm to the human masses.

A Funny "Shrinking Rhyme Story" 280

— Shi Ben

Not long ago, the "Chunqiu" column of this newspaper published an article by Mr. X called "Words Under the Leaves," which was witty and unparalleled, and the wonderful words eased the mood. "Words Under the Leaves" are commonly called "Shrinking Rhymes." In Pudong and other places, the middle and lower classes are all capable of this. They often like to use "Shrinking Rhymes" to joke when working or resting. For example, if you want to take advantage of someone, you say, "You have to call me (City God)!" or "You are my (cigarette brand)!" etc. Often without thinking, they blurt out something funny. The other night, when I was cooling off, I talked to Mr. X, a tailor next door, about "Shrinking Rhymes." He told a story about "Shrinking Rhymes," which was quite amusing, so I recorded it and submitted it to this publication to make the readers laugh.

He said, "In the past, there was a certain person named A, who was quite humorous and knew the words under the leaves." One day, he and his companions were playing in a temple. He happened to see a beautiful young woman,盛裝豔服, coming to the temple to burn incense. He stepped forward to take a closer look and saw that although the young woman's appearance was beautiful, the pair of golden lotuses under her榴裙 were as big as a rough man! It was really a flaw in the beauty. So he said to his companion, "A 'cow head horse' (face), although 'killing to ask' (good), but those 'nail-hammering turns' (feet), so 'straight waist folds' (big), is really half a Guanyin!" The young woman heard it, understood that he was saying bad things about her, but did not say anything. After burning incense, she got into the sedan chair and left. Who knew that this young woman was the beloved concubine of the magistrate of this county? She went back and told her husband about A's humiliating words and cried to her husband. The magistrate was furious when he heard it and thought that A had intentionally insulted the official's family. He immediately ordered the bailiffs to go directly to the temple to arrest A. The magistrate personally interrogated him and said to A, "Since you are good at glib tongue and playing with words, this county will not punish you for the time being. I will give you a limit to say five 'true' words in 'Shrinking Rhymes.' If you say them correctly, I will release you. If you say them incorrectly, I will investigate you again." A heard it and thought that there was nothing difficult in this, so he quickly replied, "Ten thousand diseases one" (rhymes with true), "A piece of sky" (true), "Hu Da Tian" (rhymes with true), "Yuan Shi Tian" (rhymes with true). Who knew that there was still one, and he could not think of it after a hundred thoughts. So the magistrate ordered him to be thrown into prison, and he would be released after he had said five words. A cried and cried in prison, thinking day and night, but it was difficult to think of it. Later, his wife came to visit him in prison. The husband and wife met and cried together! A told how it started, how he was arrested, and how he could not get out of prison. When his wife heard it, she knew that the disaster was caused by teasing and joking, and it was really a fake thing that turned into a real thing. So she blurted out, "Why did it turn from fake to true?" Who knew that when A heard these words, he was overjoyed and shouted, "Good (turning from fake to)!" He had been thinking for a long time but could not think of a true word. Now he got it effortlessly in nothingness, so he immediately reported it to the magistrate and was released.

Childhood Companion 281

— Ping

Random Notes from Hometown, Part 1

I haven't seen my hometown for a long time. Sitting in a rickshaw from the train station, I seemed to be nestled in my mother's arms, letting the rickshaw shake forward, making beautiful childhood dreams. Although there were many new buildings and changed streets, which were no longer as simple as when I left, I could see my hometown again, and I couldn't describe the emotions of joy and sorrow for a while.

The rickshaw was about to reach the gate of my house, and it was already twilight. The [tree] in front of the gate, waving its leafy claws, made the row of old houses even more desolate. The wheat field was no longer the same as before. A three- or five-year-old child was playing with something at the base of the tree, and an old woman in front of the low house was scolding him angrily. It was only when my rickshaw approached that I recognized that the old woman was A Niu's mother. She seemed to know that I was back, and said, "Young Master is really back!" Saying this, she called out to the child, "Hurry up and call your dad!"

I ordered the rickshaw to stop. I wanted to ask her who the child was, but the child had already led Zhi Niu's hand out of the house next door.

"Young Master is back. Xiao Niu, this is the landlord's young master." He held the child's hand, but the child slipped away to the base of the tree.

A Niu was our childhood friend. Catching sparrows, catching cicadas, we often argued over a small matter; as for crying with a face full of grievances and shouting for his mother, there were also times. Now that I have been away from my hometown for a few years, he has also taken up the hoe to cultivate his fields. You see, with a red and black face, bare chest, revealing the muscles he has trained from labor, and the pants rolled up to his thighs, compared with my 풍삼 comrade, and he also rented our small house, he seems to feel the disparity in our status, but I also seem to be very uncomfortable with his humble appearance. Starting a conversation, I said, "Is that your son?"

"Young Master is. He can't be seen!" He seemed to force a smile on his face, concealing the unnaturalness of his speech.

"Dad, a cicada." The child caught the animal at the base of the tree and happily showed it to his dad.

"Go to sleep, catching cicadas every day." A Niu scolded the child, and said with a smile, "Young Master, have you not eaten yet? I'll come over in a while."

"Come over and talk in a while." I said goodbye to the three of them and went to my own home.

That night, there was a dispute in the family. Although I was a dumb puppet for two hours, I was very unhappy about the family drama that was often staged over a bit of inheritance. I wanted to return to Shanghai that night, but I couldn't get away before my puppet work was over. (This matter is detailed in Part 2 of the Random Notes from Hometown)

Sleeping in the broken house like an ancient temple, I didn't sleep well in the middle of the night. I heard the wind blowing over the roof, and the rats squeaking in the corner of the house. Finally, A Niu's red and black face floated to my front, and he had been taken away by age, and he knew how to call "Young Master." Catching locusts, catching cicadas, it was already his son's era. If you talk about the story of him crying and telling his mother for a locust shell, A Niu doesn't know whether to cry or laugh? We are still not thirty years old, and the companions of the same era have already torn up such a deep gap, so decades later, the inheritance will cause disputes among the descendants.

I fell asleep before dawn, but A Niu's red and black face did not disappear from my dreams.
